One Paternal Uncle and Two Maternal Uncles: Distribution of Bequest to 'Aqarib'
Distribution when only one paternal and two maternal uncles exist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a plural term in a bequest requires at least two recipients and calculate the shares when only one individual from one category survives.

Core Idea
A plural term (sighah al-jam') in a bequest necessitates at least two recipients; a single category member cannot take the whole.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in bequest law: when a testator makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' (relatives) but only has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles as heirs. The key legal principle is that the plural word 'aqarib' requires a minimum of two recipients, so the single paternal uncle cannot take the entire bequest. Instead, he receives half, and the two maternal uncles collectively take the other half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Plural Term
The testator bequeaths to 'aqarib', a plural form meaning relatives. The surviving relatives are one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. Note that 'aqarib' is a sighah al-jam' (plural construct).
The plural form is critical because its meaning imposes a minimum number of recipients.
2
Apply the Rule: Plural Requires at Least Two
In Hanafi law, when a bequest is made using a plural term, it must be distributed such that at least two individuals receive a share. Since the paternal uncle is alone, he cannot take the whole bequest.
This rule is analogous to inheritance law (mirath) where plural terms also require a minimum of two.
3
Distribute the Bequest Accordingly
The paternal uncle, being one person, receives half of the bequest. The remaining half goes to the two maternal uncles, who together form a group satisfying the plural condition.
The maternal uncles take as a group; they do not each take an individual share from the half, but collectively own it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موصی نے اقرباء کیلئے وصیت کی اور فقط چا اور دو ماموں ہیں حکم
ولو ترک عما و خالین فللعم نصف الوصية والنصف للخالين لانه لا بد من اعتبار معنى الجمع وهو الاثنان في الوصية كما في الميراث
ترجمہ اور اگر موصی نے ایک چا اور ماموں چھوڑے تو چچا کے لئے وصیت کا نصف ہے اور نصف دونوں ماموں کے لئے اس لئے کہ جمع کے معنی کا اعتبار ضروری ہے اور وہ وصیت میں دو ہیں جیسے میراث میں۔
تشریح اگر موصی نے اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی تھی اور اس نے فقط ایک چا اور دو ماموں چھوڑے ہیں تو چونکہ اقرباء جمع کا صیغہ ہے جس کے لئے کم از کم دو افراد درکار ہیں اور چچا صرف ایک ہے اس لئے وہ چچا صرف نصف کا حقدار ہوگا اور نصف بچ گیا تو اس کو دونوں ماموں میں گئے۔
Ruling: The testator made a bequest for his relatives, and he left only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. And if he leaves one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of the bequest, and half for the two maternal uncles, because it is necessary to consider the meaning of plurality, and that is two in the bequest, as in inheritance. Translation: And if the testator leaves one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of the bequest, and half for the two maternal uncles, because consideration of the meaning of plural is necessary, and that is two in the bequest as in inheritance. Explanation: If the testator made a bequest for his relatives and he left only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then since 'aqarib' is a plural form requiring at least two individuals, and the paternal uncle is only one, he is entitled to only half. The remaining half goes to the two maternal uncles.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling for a specific scenario: when the testator makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' (plural) but the surviving relatives are only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. Since the term 'aqarib' is plural, it necessitates at least two recipients. The paternal uncle is only one person, so he cannot take the entire bequest by himself. Therefore, he receives half of the bequest, and the remaining half goes to the two maternal uncles, who together constitute a plural number. This is analogous to inheritance law where plural forms require at least two. The key principle is that the plural word 'aqarib' imposes a minimum of two recipients, and if only one of a certain category exists, that category cannot take the whole.

Key Terms
جمع کا صیغہ (sighah al-jam'): The plural form, here 'aqarib', requiring at least two individuals for its application.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to his 'aqarib' and leaves only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, what share does the paternal uncle receive?
A) The entire bequest.
B) Half of the bequest.
C) One third of the bequest.
D) Nothing, because he is alone.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest uses a plural term like 'aqarib', it must be distributed to at least two recipients; a single individual cannot take the whole.

Singular vs Plural Wording in Bequests to Relatives
Difference in distribution when using singular vs plural wording in bequests to relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests using singular wording and apply it to identify the recipient.

Core Idea
Singular 'dhi qarabati' gives all to the closest relative; plural requires distribution.

This lesson examines how a single word choice in a bequest — singular vs plural — radically changes the distribution. The Hanafi school treats the wording literally, leading to different outcomes even with the same set of relatives. Understanding this distinction is crucial for drafting valid wills and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording
Determine whether the testator used a singular term like 'dhi qarabati' (my relative) or a plural term like 'aqaribi' (my relatives).
2
Determine the closest relative
Among the testator's relatives, identify the single closest relative based on kinship proximity. In the example, the paternal uncle is closer than maternal uncles.
Hanafi inheritance rules determine closeness.
3
Apply the singular ruling
If singular, the entire bequest goes to that single closest relative. No distribution among multiple relatives.
Contrast with plural which requires at least two recipients.
4
Note the exclusion
All other relatives besides the closest are excluded from the bequest. In the example, maternal uncles receive nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد کا صیغہ استعمال کرنے کی صورت میں کون سا اقرب شمار کیا جائے گا
بخلاف ما اذا اوصى لذى قرابته حيث يكون للعم كل الوصية لان اللفظ للفرد فيحرز الواحد كلها اذهو الاقرب
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ موصی نے اپنے قرابت والے کے لئے وصیت کی ہو اس حیثیت ہے کہ پوری وصیت چچا کے لئے ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہ واحد کا لفظ ہے پس ایک پوری وصیت کو لے گا اس لئے کہ یہی اقرب ہے۔
تشریح اگر موصی نے جمع کا صیغہ اقرباء استعمال نہ کیا ہو بلکہ واحد کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہو یعنی یوں کہا ہو کہ میرے قرابت والے کیلئے صیت ہے تو اب فقط چا تجھے پوری وصیت کا حقدار ہوگا اور دونوں ماموں بالکل وصیت سے محروم ہو نگے کیونکہ یہاں اکیلا چاہی اقرب
Which relative will be considered when using the singular form? Contrary to the case when he makes a bequest for 'dhi qarabati' (his relative, singular), then the entire bequest is for the paternal uncle, because the word is for an individual, so the one takes all, as he is the closest. Translation: Contrary to the case when the testator made a bequest for his relative (singular), then in that situation the entire bequest will be for the paternal uncle, because it is a singular word; thus the one will take the whole bequest, because he is the closest. Explanation: If the testator did not use the plural form 'aqarib' but used the singular, i.e., he said 'for my relative', then only the paternal uncle will be entitled to the entire bequest, and the two maternal uncles will be completely deprived, because here the single paternal uncle is the closest.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage highlights the critical difference in outcome based on the wording used in the bequest. If the testator says 'for my relative' (singular: dhi qarabati), then only one relative, the closest one, receives the entire bequest. In the scenario with one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, the paternal uncle is the closest relative, so he takes everything. This contrasts with the previous lesson where using the plural 'aqarib' required at least two recipients. The principle is that singular wording directs the bequest to the single nearest relative, while plural wording necessitates distribution among at least two. The practical impact is significant: maternal uncles get nothing if singular is used, whereas they share if plural is used.

Key Terms
ذی قرابته (dhi qarabati): Singular 'my relative', directing the bequest to one individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'I bequeath to my relative' (singular) and he has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, who receives the bequest?
A) The paternal uncle gets everything.
B) The two maternal uncles get everything.
C) All three share equally.
D) The bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The use of singular vs plural wording in a bequest to relatives radically changes the distribution: singular gives all to the single closest relative.

Wasiyyah to 'Ahl' of a Person: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'ahl' in a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the differing interpretations of 'ahl' in a will between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn, and apply the Hanafi usul rule of mutlaq to determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For a will to 'ahl', Abu Hanifa says wife only; Sahibayn include all dependents — the dispute turns on literal vs customary meaning.

This passage examines a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement on the meaning of 'ahl' in a will (wasiyyah). While both views are rooted in the Hanafi school, they lead to different distributions of the testator's property. Understanding the reasoning helps you see how the school handles linguistic ambiguity using usul principles.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify what each position claims about the beneficiaries of the will. Abu Hanifa: only the wife. Sahibayn: all dependents (wife, children, servants).
2
Identify the linguistic and textual proofs
For Abu Hanifa: Quran 28:29 (Musa travels with his 'ahl' meaning wife) and Arabic usage 'tahhala' meaning to marry. For Sahibayn: Quran 12:93 (Yusuf says 'bring me your ahl' including all family) and custom (urf).
These verses are the key dalil naqli for each side.
3
Analyze the usul principle of mutlaq
The Hanafi rule: an absolute word (mutlaq) must be taken in its literal meaning unless a contextual indicator (qarina) shifts it. Abu Hanifa argues no qarina here; Sahibayn argue custom itself is a qarina.
This is the core methodological difference.
4
Compare the role of custom (urf)
Sahibayn rely on urf to broaden the meaning. Abu Hanifa insists on the literal unless clear evidence. See how each side weighs urf against the mutlaq principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: who gets the property. Later Hanafi scholars prefer Sahibayn due to custom and the Yusuf verse, making their view the mufta bihi (operative position).
Both opinions remain valid but the preferred one is widely applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلاں کے اہل کیلئے وصیت کی تو کون مصداق ہوگا ، اقوال فقہا
قال و من اوصى لاهل فلان فهى على زوجته عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يتناول من يعولهم و تضمهم نفقته اعتبارا للعرف وهو مؤيد بالنص قال الله تعالى و اتونی باهلكم اجمعين وله ان اسم الاهل حقيقة في الزوجة يشهد بذالک قوله تعالی و سار باهله ومنه قولهم تاهل ببلدة كذا و المطلق ينصرف الى الحقيقة ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور جس نے فلاں کے اہل کے لئے وصیت کی تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وصیت اس کی زوجہ پر محمول ہوگی اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ان لوگوں کو شامل ہو گی جو اسکی عیال میں ہیں اور جن کو اس کا نفقہ ملتا ہے عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور نص سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے " و أتونی با هلکم اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اہل زوج کے اندر حقیقت ہے فرمان باری تعالی و سار باھلہ اس کا شاہد ہے اور اس سے ان کا قول ہے "تأهل ببلدة كذا " اور مطلق کامل کی جانب منصرف ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ فلاں کے اہل کو میرا اتنا مال دید یا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اہل سے مراد ز وجہ ہوگی اور وہی وصیت کی حقدار ہوگی ، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اہل میں وہ تمام لوگ داخل ہیں جو زید کی عیال میں داخل ہوں اور زیدان کے نفقہ کا ذمہ دار ہو جیسے بیوی بچے اور غلام و خادم وغیرہ ۔ صاحبین نے عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے یہ بات کہی ہے کہ عرف میں یہ تمام لوگ اہل میں داخل ہوتے ہیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت یوسف کا یہ قول نقل کیا ہے و آتونی با هلكم اجمعین جو انھوں نے اپنے بھائیوں سے کہا تھا کہ تم اپنے اہل وعیال کو میرے پاس لے آؤ تو یہاں اہل میں سب داخل ہیں یعنی بیوی اور بچے اور غلام و خادم وغیرہ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اہل کے حقیقی معنی زوجہ کے ہیں اور دوسروں پر بطریق مجاز بولا جاتا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت موسی کے بارے میں ارشاد فرمایا ہے و سار باهله ، یعنی وہ اپنی بیوی کو لے چلے ، اور اہل عرب کا قول ہے "تأهل ببلده كذا ، یعنی فلاں شہر میں اہل بنایا یعنی زوجہ نکاح میں لی۔ اور جب لفظ مطلق بولا جاتا ہے اور کوئی ایسا قرینہ نہ ہو جو اس کو معنی مجازی کی طرف پھیرے دے تو لفظ سے اس کے حقیقی معنی مراد ہوا کرتے ہیں اور اگر کوئی قرینہ موجود ہو جیسے حضرت یوسف کے کلام میں تو معنی مجازی مراد لیے جاتے ہیں۔
And whoever makes a will for the 'ahl' of so-and-so: according to Abu Hanifa, it applies to his wife. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it includes those whom he supports and whose maintenance he guarantees, considering custom, and it is supported by the text: Allah says 'and bring me your families all together' (12:93). And for him (Abu Hanifa), the word 'ahl' is literal for wife, as evidence by His saying 'and travel with his family' (27:10) and their saying 'he took a wife in such a city'. And the absolute is turned to the literal meaning. Explanation: Zaid made a will saying 'give my property to the ahl of so-and-so.' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, ahl means wife, and she is entitled to the will. According to Sahibayn, ahl includes all those who are dependents of Zaid and for whom he is responsible for maintenance, such as wife, children, slaves, servants, etc. Sahibayn said this based on custom, that in custom all these people are included in ahl, and Allah narrated the saying of Prophet Yusuf 'bring me your families all together', where ahl includes everyone – wife, children, slaves, servants. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the literal meaning of ahl is wife, and it is used metaphorically for others. Allah said about Prophet Musa 'and travel with his family', meaning he took his wife, and the Arabs say 'tahhala bi-baladin kaza' meaning 'he married in such a city'. And when the absolute word is used without any contextual indicator that turns it to the metaphorical meaning, the literal meaning is intended. If there is a contextual indicator like in the speech of Yusuf, then the metaphorical meaning is intended.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the word 'ahl' (family) in a will. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when someone makes a will for 'ahl' of a person, it refers exclusively to his wife. This is based on the literal meaning of 'ahl' as wife, supported by Quranic usage (Surah al-Qasas 28:29, where 'ahl' refers to Musa's wife) and Arabic linguistic convention. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree, holding that 'ahl' includes all dependents for whom the person is responsible, such as wife, children, and servants. They base this on custom (urf) and a broader interpretation of the Quranic verse where Yusuf says 'bring me your ahl' (Surah Yusuf 12:93), which includes not just wives but children and others. The commentator explains that the dispute hinges on whether the word is used literally or metaphorically when absolute. Abu Hanifa insists on the literal meaning unless there is a contextual indicator (qarina) that points to the metaphorical meaning. The passage clarifies that both positions are respected within the Hanafi school, and the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) may vary by context.

Key Terms
اهل (ahl): Family; specifically in this dispute: either wife alone (Abu Hanifa) or all dependents (Sahibayn).
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute or unqualified word; in this context, the word 'ahl' used without a qarina (contextual indicator).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn, when someone makes a will for the 'ahl' of a person, who is included?
A) Only the wife
B) Only the children
C) All dependents including wife, children, and servants
D) The entire tribe

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a will uses 'ahl' without qualification, the default interpretation favored by later scholars includes all dependents, not just the wife.

Wasiyyah to 'Al' and 'Ahl al-Bayt' of a Person
Ruling on the interpretation of 'al' and 'ahl al-bayt' in a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of 'al' and 'ahl al-bayt' in a will and explain the scope of beneficiaries included in each term.

Core Idea
In a will, 'al' means the paternal tribe excluding offspring of daughters; 'ahl al-bayt' explicitly includes the father and grandfather.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school interprets two key terms — 'al' and 'ahl al-bayt' — when they appear in a wasiyyah. Understanding these distinctions ensures that the testator's intent is fulfilled correctly within the confines of Islamic law. The passage from Al-Hidayah provides clear linguistic reasoning and examples.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two terms
Identify that the passage treats 'al' and 'ahl al-bayt' as distinct. 'Al' is interpreted as 'ahl al-bayt' but with specific exclusions; 'ahl al-bayt' has its own explicit inclusion of ancestors.
The translation clarifies that 'al' is the tribe to which a person is attributed.
2
Understand the linguistic basis for 'al'
Recognize that 'al' linguistically means the tribe of attribution. The Hanafi ruling equates 'al' with 'ahl al-bayt' but limits it to paternal relatives, excluding descendants of daughters and sisters.
The reasoning is based on customary usage ('urf').
3
Identify the specific inclusions and exclusions
For 'al': all paternal tribe members except children of daughters/sisters. For 'ahl al-bayt': explicitly includes father and grandfather as the origin of the house.
The exclusion of offspring of daughters/sisters is a Hanafi specificity.
4
Apply to a hypothetical example
Use the example of Imam Zain al-Abidin: a will for his 'al' includes his entire paternal tribe but not the children of his daughters or sisters. A will for his 'ahl al-bayt' includes his father and grandfather.
This demonstrates the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لفظ آل فلاں سے وصیت کا حکم
ولو اوصى لأل فلان فهو لاهل بيته لان الال القبيلة التي ينسب اليها ولو اوصى لاهل بيت فلان يدخل فيه ابوه وجده لان الاب اصل البيت
ترجمہ ۔ اور اگر اس نے ال فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی تو یہ وصیت اس کے اہل بیت کے لئے ہوگی اس لئے کہ ال وہ قبیلہ ہے جس کی جانب وہ شخص منسوب کیا جاتا ہے اور اگر اس نے فلاں کے اہل بیت کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس میں فلاں کا باپ اور اس کا دادا داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ باپ بیت کی اصل ہے۔
تشریح اگر زید نے مثلا ال خالد کے لئے وصیت کی تو خالد کے گھرانے اور خاندان کے لوگ اس میں داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ یہاں ال سے وہ قبیلہ ہے جس کی جانب خالد کی نسبت ہوتی ہے، مثلاً اول امام زین العابدین کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس سے مراد ان کا گھرانہ ہو گا یعنی پورا قبیلہ یعنی اولا دعلی میں سے جو مذکر ہیں وہ اور جو مؤنث ہیں البتہ بنات واخوات کی اولا داس میں شامل نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر زید نے خالد کے اہل بیت کے لئے وصیت کی تو خالد کا گھرانہ اس وصیت میں داخل ہوگا اور خالد کے باپ دادا بھی اس وصیت میں داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ گھرانہ کی اصل تو باپ دادا ہی ہیں۔
Ruling on wasiyyah to the 'al' of so-and-so. And if he makes a will for the 'al' of so-and-so, it is for his 'ahl al-bayt' (household), because 'al' is the tribe to which he is attributed. And if he makes a will for the 'ahl al-bayt' of so-and-so, his father and grandfather are included, because the father is the origin of the house. Translation: If he makes a will for the 'al' of so-and-so, it is for his household because 'al' is the tribe to which he is attributed. And if he makes a will for the 'ahl al-bayt' of so-and-so, his father and grandfather are included because the father is the foundation of the household. Explanation: If Zaid makes a will for the 'al' of Khalid, then Khalid's family and clan are included, because 'al' here means the tribe to which Khalid is attributed. For example, if someone makes a will for the 'al' of Imam Zain al-Abidin, it refers to his household, i.e., the entire tribe – all males and females, but the children of daughters and sisters are not included. And if Zaid makes a will for the 'ahl al-bayt' of Khalid, then Khalid's household is included, and also his father and grandfather because the origin of the household is the father and grandfather.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage explains the legal interpretation of the words 'al' and 'ahl al-bayt' in the context of a will. When a testator uses the word 'al' (family/tribe) of a specific person, it is understood to mean his 'ahl al-bayt' (household), which includes all those who are part of his lineage and tribe. However, the commentator specifies that this does not include the offspring of daughters and sisters (i.e., those who are not paternal blood relatives). On the other hand, if the testator uses the term 'ahl al-bayt' (people of the house), then the father and grandfather are explicitly included because they are considered the foundation of the household. The reasoning is linguistic and based on customary usage. These rulings help clarify the scope of a will when ambiguous terms are used, ensuring the testator's intention is honored within the framework of Hanafi legal principles.

Key Terms
آل (al): Tribe or family to which a person is attributed; in a will, it refers to the ahl al-bayt (household).
اهل البيت (ahl al-bayt): Household; includes the person's father and grandfather as the origin of the house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone makes a will for the 'ahl al-bayt' of Zaid, who is included?
A) Zaid's wife and children only
B) Zaid's father and grandfather
C) All Zaid's dependents
D) Zaid's entire tribe

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'al' in a will refers to the paternal tribe excluding descendants of females, while 'ahl al-bayt' explicitly includes the testator's father and grandfather.

The Meaning of 'Nasab' and 'Jins' in a Will
Ruling on the interpretation of nasab and jins in wills

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'nasab', 'jins', and 'qarabah' in the context of a will and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine the beneficiaries.

Core Idea
In a will, 'nasab' and 'jins' refer only to paternal relatives; 'qarabah' includes both sides.

When a testator uses terms like 'ahl nasab' or 'jins', the interpretation can be ambiguous. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that these terms are limited to paternal lineage, clarifying who benefits from the will. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly executing the testator's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms used in the will
Note whether the testator used 'nasab', 'jins', or 'qarabah'. Each term has a distinct legal meaning in Hanafi fiqh.
The ruling assumes the will is otherwise valid.
2
Recognize the definition of 'nasab'
The text states that 'nasab' refers to lineage through fathers. It is traced exclusively through the paternal line.
This is a linguistic and legal convention.
3
Understand 'jins' as paternal kind
A person's 'jins' is determined by his father, not his mother. Therefore, 'my jins' means the people of my father's household.
This is based on the idea that one's kind (jins) is inherited from the father.
4
Contrast with 'qarabah'
'Qarabah' is broader and includes both maternal and paternal relatives. If the testator uses 'qarabah', the will benefits all relatives.
The passage explicitly distinguishes qarabah from nasab and jins.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Consider an Alawi testator making a will for 'jinsihi'. Only those Alawis related through the paternal line are included, not those through the mother.
The example illustrates the practical effect.

ولو اوصى لاهل نسبه او لجنسه فالنسب عبارة عمن ينسب اليه والنسب يكون من جهة الاباء وجنسه اهل بيت ابيه دون امه لان الانسان يتجنس بابيه بخلاف قرابته حيث يكون من جانب الام والاب

Ruling on wasiyyah to one's 'ahl al-nasab' (people of lineage) or to one's 'jins' (kind/species). And if he makes a will for the people of his lineage or for his kind, then 'nasab' is an expression for those to whom he is attributed, and lineage is from the side of fathers. And his kind is the people of his father's household, not his mother's, because a person is of the kind of his father, unlike his qarabah (relatives) which are from both mother's and father's sides. Translation: If he makes a will for his relatives of lineage or his kind, then 'nasab' means those to whom he is attributed, and lineage is from the side of fathers. His 'jins' is the people of his father's household, not his mother's, because a person takes his kind from his father, unlike his qarabah which includes both sides. Explanation: If Zaid makes a will for his ahl nasab or for his jins, in both cases, the will includes those members of his household whose lineage connects to the same ancestor to whom the testator traces his lineage. For example, if an Alawi makes a will saying 'this is for my ahl nasab or for my jins', then it includes those whose lineage traces to Ali, i.e., from the father's side, they are Alawis, because lineage is considered from the father's side, not the mother's. And by 'jins' is meant his father's household. Because a person is of the same kind as his father's household, not his mother's household. And qarabah is general for both, so ahl qarabah includes people from the father's side and the mother's side.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between the terms 'nasab' (lineage), 'jins' (kind/species), and 'qarabah' (relatives) in the context of a will. According to the Hanafi school, when a testator makes a will for 'ahl nasabihi' (people of his lineage) or 'jinsihi' (his kind), the beneficiaries are limited to his paternal relatives only, i.e., those who share his paternal ancestry. This is because nasab is traced through the father's side, and jins is determined by the father. In contrast, if he uses the term 'qarabah', it includes both maternal and paternal relatives. The example given is of an Alawi (descendant of Ali) making a will for his nasab or jins: only those who are Alawis through the paternal line are included, not those related through the mother. This ruling helps clarify ambiguous wills and ensures the testator's intention is correctly interpreted according to linguistic conventions and Hanafi legal principles.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage; specifically paternal lineage through fathers.
جنس (jins): Kind or species; in this context, the group defined by paternal ancestry.
قرابت (qarabah): Relatives; includes both paternal and maternal sides.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All relatives, both maternal and paternal
B) Only paternal relatives
C) Only maternal relatives
D) Only the testator's immediate family

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a will to 'ahl nasab' or 'jins' is limited to paternal relatives only.

Wasiyyah to a Group: Counted vs Uncounted
Ruling on will to a countable vs uncountable group

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a will to a group of a specific description is restricted to the poor if the group cannot be counted, and state the legal reasoning (qurbah).

Core Idea
A will for a group: if countable, all members inherit; if not, only the poor.

When a testator makes a will for a specific category of people—such as the orphans, blind, or widows of a tribe—the Hanafi school distinguishes based on whether the group can be counted. This lesson unpacks the logic: a will is a transfer of ownership (tamlik), so it only applies to identifiable individuals. If the group is too large to enumerate, the will is redirected to the poor among them, because the true objective (qurbah) is fulfilled by alleviating need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's wording
Consider the language of the will: does it specify a group by name (e.g., 'orphans of Banu Tamim') or by description? This determines whether the group is countable.
The group may be defined by tribe or by condition (orphans, blind, etc.).
2
Assess countability (ihsa)
Determine if the group is small enough that each individual can be enumerated (yuhsun). If yes, all members—rich and poor, male and female—are included. If not, proceed to step 3.
Countability is a practical question; if the group is large and indefinite, it is considered uncountable.
3
Apply the restriction to the poor
If the group is uncountable, the will is limited to the poor among them. The legal cause (illah) is that the purpose of a charitable will is qurbah, which is achieved by satisfying needs (sadd al-khallah, radd al-ju'ah).
The very description (orphan, blind, etc.) implies need, but the rich among them do not require the bequest.
4
Understand the talil (legal reasoning)
The text provides a teleological reasoning: since a will is a transfer of ownership (tamlik), it requires identifiable beneficiaries. When that's impossible due to uncountability, the default charitable purpose (qurbah) restricts the will to the needy, as they are the intended recipients of charity.
This is a classic example of combining textual interpretation with purposive reasoning (istihsan? but here it's talil from the nature of the act).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بنوفلاں کے یتیموں ، اپاہجوں، اندھوں اور بیوہ عورتوں کیلئے وصیت کا حکم
ولو اوصى لا يتام بنى فلان او لعميا نهم اولزمناهم او لا راملهم ان كانوا قوما يحصون دخل في الوصية فقراؤهم و اغنياؤهم ذكورهم واناثهم لانه امكن تحقيق التمليك فى حقهم والوصية تمليك وان كانوا لا يحصون فالوصية في الفقراء منهم لان المقصود من الوصية القربة و هى فى سد الخلة ورد الجوعة وهذا سامى تشعر بتحقق الحاجة فجاز حمله على الفقراء
Ruling on wasiyyah to orphans of Banu so-and-so, or to their blind, or to their chronically ill, or to their widows. If they are a group that can be counted, then the will includes their poor and their rich, their males and their females, because it is possible to effect ownership for them, and a will is a transfer of ownership. And if they cannot be counted, then the will is for the poor among them, because the purpose of a will is seeking closeness to Allah, and that is in fulfilling needs and satisfying hunger. And this expression indicates the reality of need, so it is permissible to restrict it to the poor.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a testator makes a will for a specific category of people, such as orphans, blind, chronically ill, or widows of a particular tribe (Banu so-and-so). The ruling distinguishes two cases: if the group is limited and can be counted (yuhsun), then all members of that group are included, regardless of their wealth or gender, because the will is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) and it is possible to distribute to each identifiable person. However, if the group is large and cannot be counted (la yuhsun), then the will is restricted to the poor among them. The reasoning is that the purpose of a will is to achieve closeness to Allah (qurbah), which is primarily realized by fulfilling the needs of the poor – supplying their necessities and alleviating their hunger. The commentator notes that the very mention of such categories (orphans, blind, etc.) implies need, so it is appropriate to limit the will to the needy. This rule balances the testator's intention to benefit the specified group with the practical limitations of distribution.

Key Terms
بني فلان (bani fulan): The tribe or clan of so-and-so; a group of people related by patrilineal descent.
يحصون (yuhsun): Can be counted; a group small enough for individuals to be enumerated.
قربة (qurbah): Act of seeking closeness to Allah; the religious purpose of a charitable will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone makes a will for the orphans of Banu Tamim, and the orphans are numerous and cannot be counted, who receives the bequest?
A) All orphans, rich and poor
B) Only the poor orphans
C) Only the wealthy orphans
D) The will is invalid

Key Takeaway
A will to a group that is uncountable is restricted to the poor, based on the purpose of qurbah; a countable group includes all members regardless of wealth.

The Hanafi Interpretation of 'Ahl Bayt' in Wills
States the ruling on who is included in a will for ahl bayt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi interpretation of 'ahl bayt' in wills and identify who is included and excluded.

Core Idea
'Ahl bayt' in a will means patrilineal household; father and grandfather are the foundation.

When a testator makes a will for the 'ahl bayt' of a person, the Hanafi school has a specific interpretation. This lesson clarifies that 'ahl bayt' refers to the patrilineal lineage, with the father and grandfather as the core members, and excludes certain descendants like children of daughters and sisters. Understanding this definition is crucial for correctly implementing such wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
The passage addresses how the term 'ahl bayt' (household) is interpreted in a will. Determine what the testator intended and how the Hanafi school defines it.
The will is made to the 'ahl bayt' of a specified person, e.g., Zaid's 'ahl bayt'.
2
Extract the Core Ruling
The passage states that the father and grandfather are included in the will because the father is the foundation of the household. This is the key ruling.
Other patrilineal relatives may also be included, but the father and grandfather are specifically mentioned.
3
Analyze the Examples
The commentary provides two examples: (1) a will for 'al Khalid' includes Khalid's tribe; (2) a will for the family of Imam Zayn al-Abidin includes all descendants of Ali except children of daughters and sisters.
The examples clarify the scope and exclusions.
4
Understand the Rationale
The rationale is that 'ahl bayt' is based on patrilineage. The father is the origin ('asl') of the house, so he and his line (father, grandfather) are the primary beneficiaries.
This distinguishes Hanafi interpretation from schools that include matrilineal relatives.
5
Apply the Ruling
Given a hypothetical will, determine who is included based on the Hanafi definition. Exclude children of daughters and sisters (unless otherwise specified).
Practice with a scenario: Zaid makes a will for the 'ahl bayt' of Ali. Who receives?

جانب وہ شخص منسوب کیا جاتا ہے اور اگر اس نے فلاں کے اہل بیت کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس میں فلاں کا باپ اور اس کا دادا داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ باپ بیت کی اصل ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے مثلا ال خالد کے لئے وصیت کی تو خالد کے گھرانے اور خاندان کے لوگ اس میں داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ یہاں ال سے وہ قبیلہ ہے جس کی جانب خالد کی نسبت ہوتی ہے، مثلاً اول امام زین العابدین کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس سے مراد ان کا گھرانہ ہو گا یعنی پورا قبیلہ یعنی اولا دعلی میں سے جو مذکر ہیں وہ اور جو مؤنث ہیں البتہ بنات واخوات کی اولا داس میں شامل نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر زید نے خالد کے اہل بیت کے لئے وصیت کی تو خالد کا گھرانہ اس وصیت میں داخل ہوگا اور خالد کے باپ دادا بھی اس وصیت میں داخل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ گھرانہ کی اصل تو باپ دادا ہی ہیں۔
The person is attributed to a side, and if he made a will for the household (ahl bayt) of so-and-so, then the father and grandfather of so-and-so are included in it, because the father is the foundation of the house. Explanation: For example, if Zaid made a will for 'al Khalid', then Khalid's family and tribe are included, because here 'al' refers to the tribe to which Khalid is attributed. For instance, if he made a will for the family of Imam Zayn al-Abidin, then it means his household, i.e., the entire tribe, meaning the descendants of Ali, both male and female, except that the children of daughters and sisters are not included in it. And if Zaid made a will for the household of Khalid, then Khalid's family is included in this will, and Khalid's father and grandfather are also included because the foundation of the family is the father and grandfather.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling concerning the interpretation of the term 'ahl bayt' in wills. It clarifies that when a testator makes a will for the 'ahl bayt' of a specified person, the ruling of the Hanafi school is that the father and grandfather of that person are included. The rationale given is that the father is the origin of the household. In the commentary, the author expands by using examples: if Zaid makes a will for 'al Khalid', the entire tribe of Khalid is included because 'al' indicates the tribe of attribution. Similarly, if the testator makes a will for the family of Imam Zayn al-Abidin, it includes all male and female descendants of Ali, but excludes children of daughters and sisters. The key principle is that 'ahl bayt' refers to the patrilineal lineage, and thus the father and grandfather are the core members.

Key Terms
اہل بیت (ahl bayt): In the context of this will, 'ahl bayt' refers to the household of a person, including his father and grandfather as the foundation, and generally includes the patrilineal family.
ال (al): The Arabic particle used to indicate the tribe or clan when attached to a name, e.g., 'al Khalid' means the tribe of Khalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wills, 'ahl bayt' means the patrilineal household, with father and grandfather as fundamental beneficiaries.

Defining 'Nasab' and 'Jins' in a Will: The Hanafi Interpretation
Defines the scope of 'ahl nasab' and 'jins' in a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'nasab', 'jins', and 'qarabah' in the context of a will, and apply the Hanafi rule to determine which relatives are included.

Core Idea
A will for 'nasab' or 'jins' includes only paternal relatives; maternal relatives require the term 'qarabah'.

When a testator uses terms like 'ahl nasab' or 'jins' in their will, the legal effect depends on the precise definition of these terms. The Hanafi school strictly limits these terms to paternal lineage. This passage explains the definitions and contrasts them with the broader term 'qarabah', which includes both paternal and maternal relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Locate the three key terms in the passage: nasab, jins, and qarabah. Note that the passage defines the first two and contrasts them with the third.
These terms have specific legal meanings that may differ from everyday usage.
2
Define 'nasab' and 'jins'
According to the passage, 'nasab' refers to those to whom a person is attributed through his fathers (paternal lineage). 'Jins' refers to the people of his father's household, again exclusively paternal.
The reason given: 'a person takes his jins from his father'.
3
Contrast with 'qarabah'
The passage explicitly states that 'qarabah' (kinship) is general and includes both the mother's side and the father's side. This is the opposite of 'nasab' and 'jins', which are restricted to the paternal side.
Understanding this contrast is crucial for correctly interpreting a will.
4
Apply to an example
Consider the example in the commentary: an Alawi testator wills to his 'ahl nasab' or 'jins'. Only those whose lineage connects to Ali through the father's side (Alawis) are included. Maternal relatives are excluded.
This concrete example illustrates the rule in action.

ولو اوصى لاهل نسبه او لجنسه فالنسب عبارة عمن ينسب اليه والنسب يكون من جهة الاباء وجنسه اهل بيت ابيه دون امه لان الانسان يتجنس بابيه بخلاف قرابته حيث يكون من جانب الام والاب ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے اپنے ہم نسب یا اپنی جنس کے لئے وصیت کی تو نسب مراد ہے ان لوگوں سے جن کی جانب یہ منسوب کیا جاتا ہے اور نسب آباء کی جانب سے ہوا کرتا ہے اور اس کی جنس اپنے باپ کے گھرانے کے لوگ ہیں نہ کہ اس کی ماں کے گھرانے کے اس لئے کہ انسان اپنے باپ کی جنس سے ہوتا ہے بخلاف انسان کی قرابت کے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ ماں اور باپ کی جانب سے ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے اپنے اہل نسب کے لئے یا اپنی جنس کے وصیت کی تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں وصیت کے اندر اس کے گھرانے کے وہ لوگ داخل ہوں گے جن کا نسب اس شخص سے ملتا ہے جس سے موصی کا ملتا ہے مثلاً کوئی علومی وصیت کرتا ہے کہ یہ میرے اہل نسب کے لئے یا میری جنس کے لئے وصیت ہے تو اس میں وہ لوگ داخل ہوں گے جن کا نسب حضرت علی سے ملتا ہے یعنی باپ کی طرف سے وہ علوی ہوں کیونکہ نسب کا اعتبار باپ کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے ماں کی طرف سے نہیں ہوتا ، اور جنس سے بھی اس کے باپ کا گھرانہ مراد ہے۔ اس لئے کہ انسان اپنے باپ کے گھرانے کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے ماں کے گھرانے کا ہم جنس نہیں ہوتا اور قرابت دونوں کے لئے عام ہے تو اہل قرابت باپ کی طرف کے لوگ بھی ہوں گے اور ماں کی طرف کے بھی ۔
And if he made a will for his relatives by lineage (ahl nasab) or for his kind (jins), then 'nasab' refers to those to whom he is attributed, and nasab is from the side of the fathers, and his jins is the people of his father's household, not his mother's, because a person takes his jins from his father, unlike his kinship (qarabah) which is from the side of mother and father. Translation: And if he made a will for his relatives by lineage or his kind, then 'nasab' means those to whom he is attributed, and nasab is from the side of the fathers, and his jins is the people of his father's household, not his mother's, because a person takes his jins from his father, unlike his kinship which is from the side of mother and father. Explanation: If Zaid made a will for his ahl nasab or his jins, then in both cases the people of his household whose lineage connects to the one to whom the testator's lineage connects are included. For example, if an Alawi person makes a will saying 'this is for my ahl nasab' or 'for my jins', then those whose lineage connects to Ali are included, i.e., from the father's side they are Alawis, because the consideration of nasab is from the father's side, not the mother's. And by jins also his father's household is meant, because a person is of the same jins as his father's household, not his mother's household. And kinship (qarabah) is general for both, so ahl qarabah include both the father's side and the mother's side.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides a definition and ruling for the terms 'ahl nasab' and 'jins' as used in wills. The Arabic text establishes that 'nasab' refers to paternal lineage (from the fathers), and 'jins' refers to the paternal household exclusively. The commentary elaborates with an example: if an Alawi testator makes a will for his 'ahl nasab' or 'jins', only those whose lineage traces back to Ali through the father's side are included. This is because in Hanafi law, a person's lineage and kind are determined by the father, not the mother. In contrast, 'qarabah' (kinship) is broader and includes both maternal and paternal relatives. Thus, if a testator uses 'ahl nasab' or 'jins', the will benefits only the paternal relatives, not maternal ones.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): In the context of a will, 'nasab' means paternal lineage; it refers to those to whom a person is attributed through his fathers.
جنس (jins): In this will, 'jins' means the paternal household, i.e., the relatives through the father's side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator makes a will for his 'jins', who is included?
A) All his relatives including maternal
B) Only his father's household
C) Only his mother's household
D) His siblings only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'nasab' and 'jins' are strictly patrilineal; a will using these terms benefits only paternal relatives, unlike 'qarabah' which includes both sides.

Ruling for a Will Made to a Specific Group: Countability and Its Effect
States the ruling based on countability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of countability to determine who receives a will made to a specified group and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the criterion for countability.

Core Idea
A will for a specific group benefits both rich and poor if countable; if uncountable, only the poor receive.

This passage addresses a will made to a category of people (e.g., orphans of a tribe). The ruling hinges on whether the group can be counted. If countable, the testator's intent of ownership transfer (tamlik) can be fully realized, so both rich and poor are included. If uncountable, the will is restricted to the poor because the underlying purpose is closeness to Allah (qurbah) through fulfilling needs. An intra-Hanafi difference exists regarding the threshold for countability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and categories
The testator makes a will for a specific group (e.g., orphans, blind, cripples, widows) from a named tribe (e.g., Bani Fulan). Note that each category may include both poor and rich individuals.
2
Determine countability
Check if the group is countable or uncountable. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, countability is determined by the ability to count without formal census. According to Imam Muhammad, if the group exceeds 100, it is uncountable. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that it is left to the judge's discretion.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the two scenarios
If the group is countable: the will includes both rich and poor members of the described category. If uncountable: the will is restricted to the poor among them. The reason is that when ownership transfer (tamlik) is possible to all, the will is executed as intended. When it is impossible due to extreme uncertainty, the underlying objective (qurbah) is achieved by benefiting the needy.
The testator's explicit mention of 'orphans' etc. does not automatically restrict to the poor.
4
Understand the rationales
The purpose of a will is tamlik (transfer of ownership). For a countable group, it is feasible to give each a determined share. For an uncountable group, the overwhelming majority of members are poor, so limiting the will to the poor fulfills the testator's intention of qurbah.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the matter is left to the judge, with Imam Muhammad's numerical criterion (over 100) as a guideline. This is supported by Fatawa Qadikhan.
The judge may consider local circumstances.

دور کرنے میں اور یہ اسامی حاجت کے تحقق کی خبر دیتے ہیں تو اس کو فقرا ء پر محمول کرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ بنو خالد میں سے جو یتیم ہوں ان کے لئے وصیت ہے یا بنو خالد میں سے جو لوگ اندھے ہیں کہ یہ قاضی کی رائے پر موقوف ہے اور اسی پر فتویٰ ہے اور امام محمد کا قول بھی اسی کی جانب مشیر ہے۔ (کذافی فتاوی قاضیخان) تو اگر یہ لوگ قابل احصاء ہوں تو وصیت میں فقراء اور مالدار لوگ جو پانچ وغیرہ ہیں سب داخل ہوں گے اور اگر نا قابل احصاء ہوں تو فقط فقراء داخل ہونگے اور مالدار داخل نہ ہوں گے، کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ اول صورت میں ان سب کو مالک بنادینا ممکن ہے اور مالک بنا دینا ہی وصیت ہے لہذا پہلی صورت میں ثکث مال کو ان لوگوں میں سے جو ہیں خواہ فقراء یا اغنیاء سب کے درمیان برابر تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ دوسری صورت میں فقط فقر اء اس لئے داخل ہیں کہ یہاں موصی کا مقصود قربت ہے اور قربت کا مقصد یہاں یہ ہے کہ ان کی حاجت دور ہو سکے اور ان کے بھوک کی حالت دور ہو سکے اور ایتام و پانج وغیرہ یہ سب ایسے نام ہیں جو عموما فقراء ہوتے ہیں تو یہ نام ہی خود تحقیق حاجت کی جانب مشعر میں لہذا اب وصیت کو فقط فقراء And if he made a will for the orphans of Bani Fulan, or for their blind, or for their cripples, or for their widows, if they are a people who can be counted, then both their poor and their rich, their males and their females, are included in the will, because it is possible to actualize ownership (tamlik) in their right, and a will is a transfer of ownership. And if they cannot be counted, then the will is for the poor among them, because the purpose of the will is closeness to Allah (qurbah), and that is in fulfilling needs and removing hunger, and these terms indicate the realization of need, so it is permissible to restrict it to the poor. Translation: And if he made a will for the orphans of Bani Fulan, or for their blind, or for their cripples, or for their widows, if they are people who can be counted, then both their poor and their rich, their males and their females, are included in the will, because it is possible to actualize ownership in their right, and a will is a transfer of ownership. And if they cannot be counted, then the will is for the poor among them, because the purpose of the will is closeness to Allah, and that is in fulfilling needs and removing hunger, and these names indicate the realization of need, so it is permissible to restrict it to the poor. Explanation: Zaid made a will that it is for the orphans of Bani Khalid, or for the blind of Bani Khalid, or for the cripples of Bani Khalid, or for the widows of Bani Khalid. So who will be included? While some orphans are poor and some are rich, similarly some blind are poor and some are very rich, and the same applies to cripples and widows. Are all included whether poor or rich, or only the poor and needy? For this, a principle is stated: if these people, i.e., the orphans of Bani Khalid etc., are countable, then one rule applies, and if they are not countable, then another rule applies. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if they can be counted without calculation (census), they are considered countable. Imam Muhammad said that if they exceed one hundred, they are uncountable. Some scholars said it depends on the judge's opinion, and that is the fatwa, and Imam Muhammad's statement also points to that. (As in Fatawa Qadikhan). So if these people are countable, then both the poor and the rich (among the described categories) are included. If they are uncountable, then only the poor are included, and the rich are not. Why? Because in the first case, it is possible to make all of them owners, and making them owners is the very purpose of the will. Therefore, in the first case, the entire wealth is divided equally among all those who are present, whether poor or rich. In the second case, only the poor are included because here the testator's purpose is closeness to Allah, and the objective of closeness is to remove their need and alleviate their hunger. Orphans, cripples, etc., are generally poor, so these names themselves indicate the realization of need. Hence, the will is restricted to the poor.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on a will made for a specific category of people (orphans, blind, cripples, widows) from a specified tribe (Bani Fulan). The key distinction is whether the group is countable or not. If the group is countable (e.g., under 100 according to Imam Muhammad, or according to the judge's discretion), the will is valid for both rich and poor individuals of that description, because the purpose of a will is tamlik (transfer of ownership), and it is possible to give each a determined share. If the group is uncountable (e.g., more than 100), the will is restricted to the poor among them, because the testator's underlying intent is qurbah (closeness to Allah) which is achieved by fulfilling needs. The commentary includes an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Yusuf considers countability possible without formal census, while Imam Muhammad sets a numerical limit (100). The relied-upon position is that it is left to the judge's opinion, as mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan. This ruling ensures that a will is not invalidated by extreme uncertainty (jahalah fahishah) and aligns with the objectives of charity.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the act of making someone an owner. The purpose of a will is tamlik.
قربت (qurbah): Closeness to Allah; an act of devotion. Here it is interpreted as fulfilling the needs of the poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All blind people regardless of wealth

C) Only the rich among the blind
D) The will is invalid

Key Takeaway
The distribution of a will made to a specific group depends on countability: if countable, all members benefit; if uncountable, only the poor benefit.

Ruling for a Will to an Uncountable Group: The Case of 'Young Men'
States that a will for uncountable young men/women is invalid due to extreme uncertainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a will made to an uncountable group of people and explain why it is invalid due to extreme uncertainty when the term used does not indicate need.

Core Idea
A will to an uncountable group is batil if the term does not indicate need.

In the previous lesson, we saw that a will for a charitable category like 'orphans' can be validated by restricting it to the poor among them. But what if the testator uses a term like 'young men' that carries no obvious connotation of need? This lesson examines that scenario and uncovers a key principle: without an indication of need, an uncountable group makes the will void due to extreme uncertainty (jahalah mufahishah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the will's recipient category
The will is made to 'young men' (shubban) or 'young women' of a specified tribe. Note that the term does not inherently imply poverty or need.
Contrast with terms like 'orphans' or 'blind' that carry a connotation of need.
2
Determine if the group is countable
The passage states the group is uncountable (la yuhsawn). This means it is impossible to distribute shares to each individual.
If the group were small and countable, different rules might apply.
3
Check for an indication of need in the wording
The term 'young men' does not indicate need (hajah). Therefore, the will cannot be restricted to the poor among them, as was done in the previous case for 'orphans'.
Without this restriction, the will suffers from extreme uncertainty (jahalah mufahishah) and is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخاف ما اذا اوصى لشبان بني فلان وهم لا يحصون اولا یامی بنی فلان وهم لا يحصون حيث تبطل الوصية لانه ليس في اللفظ ما ينبئ عن الحاجة فلا يمكن صرفه الى الفقراء ولا يمكن تصحيحه تمليكا في حق الكل للجهالة المتفاحشة وتعذر الصرف اليهم
In contrast to the case if he made a will for the young men (shubban) of Bani Fulan, and they are uncountable, or for the young women (?) of Bani Fulan, and they are uncountable, for then the will becomes invalid (batil) because there is nothing in the wording that indicates need, so it cannot be restricted to the poor, nor can it be validated as a transfer of ownership for all due to extreme uncertainty (jahalah mufahishah) and the impossibility of distributing to them.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage contrasts with the previous ruling. Here, the testator makes a will for 'young men' (shubban) or 'young women' of a specified tribe, and the group is uncountable. The ruling is that the will is invalid (batil). The reason is that the term 'young men' or 'young women' does not inherently indicate need (hajah) – unlike 'orphans', 'blind', 'cripples', or 'widows', which typically imply need. Since there is no indication of need, the will cannot be restricted to the poor (as was done in the previous case). Moreover, because the group is uncountable, it is impossible to give each a determined share (tamlik). This creates extreme uncertainty (jahalah mufahishah) which invalidates the will. Thus, the will fails entirely. This illustrates a key principle: for a will to be valid with an uncountable group, the term used must convey a connotation of need, allowing it to be limited to the poor.

Key Terms
جهالة متفاحشة (jahalah mufahishah): Extreme uncertainty that invalidates a contract or will; here it refers to not knowing the recipients.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the testator did not specify the amount
B) Because the term does not indicate need and there is extreme uncertainty
C) Because young men cannot receive inheritances
D) Because the will is against public policy

Key Takeaway
A will to an uncountable group is batil unless the wording itself indicates a need that allows restriction to the poor.

The Countability Rule in Bequests for Needy Categories
Ruling on bequest for needy categories based on countability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests for designated categories (orphans, blind, disabled, widows) and determine whether the bequest covers all individuals or only the poor based on the countability principle.

Core Idea
A bequest to a countable group includes all, but to an uncountable group only the poor.

This lesson examines a ruling from Al-Hidayah on bequests for specific needy categories. The key question is: when a testator makes a bequest to 'the orphans of Banu Fulan' or similar, does it include both rich and poor? The answer depends on countability. The principle rests on bequest as transfer of ownership (tamlik) and the testator's intention of seeking reward by relieving need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and the ambiguity
Recognize that the bequest to orphans, blind, etc. includes both poor and rich members of that category. The ambiguity is about inclusion of rich individuals.
2
Determine countability
Assess whether the group can be enumerated (qabil al-ihsa'). If yes, tamlik to all is possible; if no, tamlik is impractical.
Imam Abu Yusuf: countable if can be counted without census; Imam Muhammad: >100 is uncountable; mufta bihi: qadi's discretion.
3
Apply the principle of tamlik
If countable, the bequest is tamlik to each individual, so all (rich and poor) are included. If uncountable, the bequest is interpreted as benefiting the needy only.
Tamlik is the fundamental nature of bequest (wasiyyah).
4
Differentiate based on qurbah
Understand that in the uncountable case, the testator's intention is qurbah (nearness to Allah) by relieving need, so the bequest is restricted to the poor.
The names (orphan, blind, widow) imply need, supporting this interpretation.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے بنو فلاں کے تیموں کے لئے یا ان کے اندھوں کے لئے یا ان کے اپاہجوں کے لئے یا ان کی بیوہ عورتوں کے لئے وصیت کی تو اگر وہ ایسے لوگ ہیں جن کو گنا جا سکتا ہو تو وصیت میں ان کے فقراء اور کون کون داخل ہوں گے۔ جب کہ بعض یتیم فقیر ہوتے ہیں اور بعض مالدار ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی کچھ اندھے غریب ہوتے ہیں اور کچھ بہت مالدار ہوتے ہیں اور اپاہجوں اور بیوگان کا بھی یہی حال ہے، تو اس وصیت میں جو یتیم اور اندھے وغیرہ ہیں سب داخل ہیں خواہ غریب ہوں یا مالدار یا فقط فقراء اور مساکین ہی داخل ہوں گے؟ تو اس کے لئے ایک اصول بیان فرمایا کہ اگر یہ لوگ یعنی بنو خالد کے ایتام وغیرہ قابل احصاء ہوں تو اور حکم ہے اور اگر قابل احصاءنہ ہوں تو اور حکم ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جب بغیر حساب و کتاب یعنی مردم شماری کے ان کا احصاء ہو سکے تو یہ قابل احصاء شمار کئے جائیں گے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر وہ سو سے زیادہ ہوں تو وہ نا قابل احصاء ہیں ، اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ یہ قاضی کی رائے پر موقوف ہے اور اسی پر فتویٰ ہے اور امام محمد کا قول بھی اسی کی جانب مشیر ہے۔ (کذافی فتاوی قاضیخان) تو اگر یہ لوگ قابل احصاء ہوں تو وصیت میں فقراء اور مالدار لوگ جو پانچ وغیرہ ہیں سب داخل ہوں گے اور اگر نا قابل احصاء ہوں تو فقط فقراء داخل ہونگے اور مالدار داخل نہ ہوں گے، کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ اول صورت میں ان سب کو مالک بنا دینا ممکن ہے اور مالک بنا دینا ہی وصیت ہے لہذا پہلی صورت میں ثلث مال کو ان لوگوں میں سے جو ہیں خواہ فقراء یا اغنیاء سب کے درمیان برابر تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ دوسری صورت میں فقط فقر اء اس لئے داخل ہیں کہ یہاں موصی کا مقصود قربت ہے اور قربت کا مقصد یہاں یہ ہے کہ ان کی حاجت دور ہو سکے اور ان کے بھوک کی حالت دور ہو سکے اور ایتام و پانج وغیرہ یہ سب ایسے نام ہیں جو عموما فقراء ہوتے ہیں تو یہ نام ہی خود تحقیق حاجت کی جانب مشعر میں لہذا اب وصیت کو فقط فقراء پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
Translation: And if he makes a bequest for the orphans of Banu Fulan, or for their blind, or for their disabled, or for their widows, then if they are people who can be counted, the bequest includes their poor and their rich, their men and their women, because transfer of ownership (tamlik) is possible with respect to them and bequest is transfer of ownership. If they cannot be counted, then the bequest is for the poor among them, because the purpose of bequest is nearness (qurbah) and nearness is in removing need and removing hunger, and these names indicate the existence of need, so it is permissible to apply it to the poor. Explanation: Zaid made a bequest: for the orphans of Banu Khalid, or for the blind of Banu Khalid, or for the disabled of Banu Khalid, or for the widows of Banu Khalid. Who will be included? While some orphans are poor and some are rich, similarly some blind are poor and some are very rich, and the same applies to disabled and widows. So in this bequest, will all orphans and blind etc. be included, whether poor or rich, or only the poor and needy? For this, a principle is stated: if these people, i.e. the orphans of Banu Khalid etc., are countable (qabil al-ihsa'), then one ruling; if they are not countable, then another ruling. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, when they can be counted without calculation i.e. census, they are considered countable. Imam Muhammad said if they are more than one hundred, they are uncountable. Some scholars said this depends on the qadi's opinion, and on this is the fatwa, and Imam Muhammad's statement also points to this. So if they are countable, the bequest includes all, poor and rich, and the bequest is divided equally among all. If they are uncountable, only the poor are included, and the rich are not. Why? Because in the first case it is possible to make all of them owners, and making them owners is the bequest itself. In the second case, only the poor are included because the testator's intention is nearness, and the purpose of nearness is to remove their need and hunger, and orphans, disabled, etc. are names that generally are poor, so these names themselves indicate need, hence the bequest is applied only to the poor.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage addresses bequests made for specific needy categories (orphans, blind, disabled, widows) of a named tribe. The ruling distinguishes between countable and uncountable numbers. If the group is small enough to be counted, the bequest includes all individuals (rich and poor) because it is possible to transfer ownership to each. Bequest is fundamentally a transfer of ownership (tamlik). If the group is too large to be counted, it is assumed the testator intended to benefit the poor only, since the purpose of such bequests is to gain reward (qurbah) by relieving need. The names (orphan, blind, etc.) imply need, so the bequest is limited to the poor. The passage then provides the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on what constitutes 'uncountable': Imam Abu Yusuf considers a group countable if it can be enumerated without a formal census; Imam Muhammad sets the threshold at one hundred; later authorities (e.g., Fatawa Qadikhan) state it is left to the qadi's discretion, which is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Key Terms
احصاء (ihsa'): The ability to count or enumerate individuals; used to determine if a bequest can cover all individuals.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the fundamental nature of a bequest according to Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a bequest is made for 'the blind of Banu Fulan' and the number of blind is uncountable, who receives the bequest?
A) All blind
B) Only the poor blind
C) Only the rich blind
D) Bequest invalid

Key Takeaway
The scope of a bequest to a category depends on countability: all if countable, only poor if uncountable.

Bequest for Uncountable Young Men or Women: Invalidity
Bequest for uncountable young men/women is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a bequest to an uncountable group of young men or women is invalid and distinguish it from a bequest to orphans or widows.

Core Idea
A bequest to an uncountable group is invalid if the term used does not indicate need.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case of bequest where the recipients are described as 'young men' or 'young women' of a tribe, and their number is uncountable. The Hanafi jurists rule that such a bequest is invalid because it suffers from extreme ignorance (jihalah mutafahishah) regarding the recipients, and the words used do not carry any implication of poverty that would allow us to restrict the bequest to the needy. This contrasts with previous cases where terms like 'orphans' or 'widows' allowed a valid interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) for 'young men of Banu Fulan' or 'young women of Banu Fulan' when they are uncountable. The ruling is that the bequest is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the dalil or reasoning
The reasoning (talil) is based on two points: (1) If we try to include all, it is impossible due to extreme ignorance (jihalah fahishah) about the number and identity. (2) If we restrict to the poor, we cannot, because the terms 'shubban' and 'adhira' do not indicate need, unlike 'orphans' or 'widows'.
The proof is implicit qiyas: a bequest requires knowledge of the recipient to be valid.
3
Contrast with the previous case
In the previous case, the bequest for orphans or widows was valid because those terms imply need, allowing restriction to the poor among them. Here, no such implication exists.
The expansion probe shows the importance of linguistic connotation.
4
Understand the concept of jihalah mutafahishah
Extreme ignorance about the recipients (uncountable numbers) makes the contract impossible to execute, so the bequest is batil. This is different from tolerable ignorance, which may be overlooked in some contracts.
Jihalah fahishah is a key invalidator in Hanafi law for contracts of tamlik.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخاف ما اذا اوصى لشبان بني فلان وهم لا يحصون اولا یامی بنی فلان وهم لا يحصون حيث تبطل الوصية لانه ليس في اللفظ ما ينبئ عن الحاجة فلا يمكن صرفه الى الفقراء ولا يمكن تصحيحه تمليكا في حق الكل للجهالة المتفاحشة وتعذر الصرف اليهم

ترجمه بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے بنو فلاں کے جوانوں کے لئے وصیت کی ہو اور وہ گنے نہیں جا سکتے یا بہنوفلاں کی جوان عورتوں کے لئے اور وہ گنی نہیں جاسکتیں اس حیثیت سے کہ وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس لفظ میں کوئی ایسی چیز نہیں ہے جو حاجت کی خبر دے تو اس کو فقراء کی جانب صرف کرنا ممکن نہ ہوگا اور نہ تمام کو مالک بنا کر اس وصیت کی تصحیح ممکن ہے شدید جہالت کی وجہ سے اور ان تمام کی جانب صرف کے متعد ر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔

تشریح زید نے بنو خالد کے نو جوانوں کے لئے یا بنو خالد کی نوجوان لڑکیوں کے لئے وصیت کی اور یہ نوجوان طبقہ اتنا وسیع ہے کہ جس کو گنا نہیں جا سکتا تو یہاں وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اگر تمام نو جوانوں کے لئے وصیت کو رکھا جائے اور تمام کو مالک بنایا جائے تو یہ متعد ر ہے چونکہ وہ ان گنت ہیں اور ان میں بے شمار ہونے کی وجہ سے شدید جہالت ہے تو یہ صورت تو ممکن نہیں ہے اور اگر ان میں سے فقط فقراء کے حق میں وصیت کبھی جائے تو یہ بھی ممکن نہیں اس لئے کہ لفظ شبان سے اور اسی طرح لفظ ایا ملی سے کچھ حاجت کے معنی مترشح نہیں ہوئے جیسے ایتام و میان سے حاجت کے معنی مترشح ہوئے تھے لہذا جب کوئی صورت باقی نہ رہے تو ہم نے مجبوراً کہا کہ وصیت باطل ہے۔
Contrast with the case where he makes a bequest for the young men of Banu Fulan and they cannot be counted, or for the young women of Banu Fulan and they cannot be counted. In that case, the bequest becomes invalid because there is nothing in the word that indicates need, so it cannot be diverted to the poor, nor can it be validated by making all owners due to extreme ignorance (jihalah) and the impossibility of distribution. Explanation: Zaid made a bequest for the young men of Banu Khalid or the young women of Banu Khalid, and this group of young people is so vast that it cannot be counted. Here the bequest becomes invalid because if we keep the bequest for all young people and make all owners, it is impossible since they are countless and there is extreme ignorance due to the uncountable number. So this is not possible. And if we only consider the poor among them, that is also not possible because the word 'shubban' (young men) and similarly 'adhira' (young women) do not give any meaning of need, unlike the words 'orphans' and 'widows' which indicated need. Therefore, when no possible interpretation remains, we say by necessity that the bequest is invalid.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage contrasts the previous ruling. If the bequest is made for 'young men' (shubban) or 'young women' (adhira) of a tribe and the number is uncountable, the bequest is invalid (batil). The reason is twofold: (1) If we try to include all young men/women, it is impossible due to the vast number causing extreme uncertainty (jihalah fahishah). (2) If we restrict to the poor only, we cannot, because the words 'young men' or 'young women' carry no inherent implication of need, unlike 'orphans' or 'widows'. Thus, there is no interpretation that can salvage the bequest, so it is void. This is in contrast to the previous case where the descriptive terms indicated need, allowing restriction to the poor.

Key Terms
شبان (shubban): Young men; a term that does not inherently imply poverty or need.
جهالة متفاحشة (jihalah mutafahishah): Extreme ignorance or uncertainty about the identity or number of recipients, which invalidates the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a bequest for the young men of a tribe invalid if they are uncountable?
A) Because the term 'young men' implies they are all poor
B) Because it is impossible to transfer ownership to all, and the term does not indicate need to restrict to the poor
C) Because the testator must specify individual names
D) Because the tribe is not specified

Key Takeaway
A bequest is invalid when the recipients are described by a term that does not indicate need and the group is uncountable, because it suffers from extreme ignorance and no valid interpretation remains.

Bequest to the Poor and Needy: Minimum Two Recipients from Each Category
Ruling statement on minimum recipients for bequest to fuqara and masakin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of recipients required for a bequest to fuqara and masakin and explain why the plural in bequests is treated as two.

Core Idea
In bequests, the plural requires at least two recipients—one is not enough.

When someone bequeaths to a group like 'the poor' (fuqara) or 'the needy' (masakin), how many must actually receive the bequest? This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi rule: the plural in bequests means a minimum of two, not three. You will learn the ruling and its practical implication for estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? The bequest (wasiyyah) to fuqara and masakin. The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) to pay the bequest to at least two individuals from each category.
The word 'wajib' here indicates a required element for fulfilling the bequest.
2
Determine the condition for fulfilling the bequest
The condition is that the number of recipients must be at least two from each group. This is based on the interpretation of the plural (jam') in the context of bequests.
In Hanafi usul, the plural generally means three, but in bequests it is reduced to two by custom (urf) and textual precedent.
3
Understand the rationale
Why two? Because the plural in bequests is given a special meaning: the minimum to represent a group is two. This is a departure from the general usul rule of three.
This ruling has been established in earlier sections of the Hidayah, forming a consistent principle.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
If Zaid bequeaths one-third of his estate to fuqara and masakin, the executor must distribute to at least two poor and two needy individuals. Giving to only one from each category would not fulfill the bequest.
The bequest is not invalidated; rather, the obligation to pay remains until two from each are satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و فى الوصية للفقراء والمساكين يجب الصرف اثنين منهم اعتباراً لمعنى الجمع واقله اثنان في الوصايا على مامر

ترجمه اور فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے وصیت کرنے میں ان میں سے دو کی جانب صرف کرنا واجب ہے جمع کے معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور جمع کا اقل فرد وصایا میں دو ہیں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر چکی ہے۔

تشریح ماقبل میں متعدد مرتبہ یہ بحث گذر چکی ہے کہ وصیت میں جمع کا اقل فرد دو ہے لہذا جب زید نے فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے وصیت کی تو ثلث کو کم از کم دو مسکین اور دو فقیر کو دینا واجب ہوگا۔
And in the bequest for the poor (fuqara) and the needy (masakin), it is obligatory to pay (the bequest) to two of them, considering the meaning of plural, and the minimum of the plural in bequests is two, as previously mentioned. Explanation: This discussion has passed multiple times that the minimum of the plural in bequests is two. Therefore, when Zaid makes a bequest for the poor and the needy, it is obligatory to give to at least two poor and two needy from the third of the estate.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: when a bequest is made to 'the poor' (fuqara) and 'the needy' (masakin), it is wajib to distribute the bequest to at least two individuals from each category. This is because in the context of bequests, the minimum number that constitutes a plural (jam') is two. This principle has been established earlier in the book. Thus, if someone bequeaths one-third of their estate to fuqara and masakin, the executor must give at least two fuqara and two masakin a share. The bequest is not fulfilled by giving to only one poor and one needy person.

Key Terms
فقراء (fuqara): The poor; those who do not have enough wealth to meet basic needs.
جمع (jam'): Plural; in Hanafi usul, the minimum of the plural is three, but in bequests (wasaya) it is two by convention.
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest; a testamentary disposition of property to take effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All poor and needy equally

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a group like 'the poor' or 'the needy' requires at least two recipients from that group to fulfill the bequest.

Bequest to Banu Fulan: Do Women Inherit?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inclusion of women in 'Banu Fulan' bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's two positions on whether 'Banu Fulan' includes women, explain the retraction based on haqiqah vs. majaz, and apply the mufta bihi position to a given bequest scenario.

Core Idea
When interpreting a bequest, the literal meaning of 'Banu' (sons) excludes women unless the term is a tribal name.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of 'Banu Fulan' in a bequest. Abu Hanifa initially included women, then retracted to include only men. The key distinction is between the literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) usage of 'Banu', and whether the term is a proper tribal name.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify Abu Hanifa's first position (including women, agreed by Sahibayn) and his final retracted position (only men).
2
Identify the dalil for each position
First position: masculine plural includes females (linguistic rule). Second position: literal meaning of 'Banu' is males, and speech defaults to literal meaning.
3
Apply the principle of haqiqah vs majaz
Understand why retraction occurred: the default is literal interpretation (haqiqah); using 'Banu' for women is metaphorical (majaz) and requires a clear indication.
4
Distinguish the tribal usage
When 'Banu Fulan' is a tribal name, it includes both men and women because it denotes affiliation, similar to 'Banu Adam'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The final position (only men) is the operative ruling unless the context indicates a tribe or clan.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text

و لو أوصى لبنى فلان يدخل فيه الاناث فى قول أبي حنيفة اول قوله وهو قولهما لان جمع الذكور يتناول الاناث ثم رجع وقال يتناول الذكور خاصة لان حقيقة الاسم للذكور وانتظامه للاناث تجوز الكلام لحقيقته بخلاف ما اذا كان بنو فلان اسم قبيلة او فخذ حيث يتناول الذكور والاناث لأنه ليس يرادبها اعيانها اذ هو تجرد الانتساب كبني ادم ولهذا يدخل فيه مولى العتاقة والموالات و حلفاؤهم

ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے بنو فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی تو ابو حنیفہ کے پہلے قول کے مطابق اور یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے اس میں عورتیں داخل ہوں گی اس لئے کہ جمع مذکر عورتوں کو شامل ہوتی ہے پھر ابوحنیفہ نے اس سے رجوع کر لیا اور فرمایا کہ فقط مردوں کو شامل ہوگا اس لئے کہ لفظ کی حقیقت مردوں کے لئے ہے اور اس کا عورتوں کو شامل ہونا بطور مجاز کے ہے اور کلام اپنی حقیقت پر محمول ہوتا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ بنو فلاں قبیلہ یافخذ کا نام ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ ( بنو فلاں ) مردوں اور عورتوں کو شامل ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس سے مراد
And if he makes a bequest for Banu Fulan, women are included according to the first statement of Abu Hanifa, and this is the statement of the two companions (Sahibayn), because the masculine plural includes women. Then Abu Hanifa retracted and said it includes only men, because the literal meaning of the name is for men, and its inclusion of women is metaphorical (majaz), and speech is applied to its literal meaning. Contrast the case when Banu Fulan is the name of a tribe or clan; then it includes both men and women because what is meant is not the individuals themselves but mere affiliation, like Banu Adam, and thus includes freed slaves and allies.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the interpretation of 'Banu Fulan' in a bequest. Abu Hanifa initially held that the term includes women, which was also the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). He later retracted this and ruled that it only includes men. The reason for the retraction is that the literal meaning (haqiqah) of the word 'banu' (sons) is male offspring, and its application to females is metaphorical (majaz). The default principle is to interpret speech literally. However, if 'Banu Fulan' is used as the proper name of a tribe or clan (like Banu Hashim), then it includes both men and women because the reference is to all descendants through affiliation (intisab), not the literal meaning of 'sons'.

Key Terms
بنو فلاں (Banu Fulan): A phrase used in bequests; whether it includes women depends on whether it is a proper tribal name or a generic reference to male descendants.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical or figurative usage of a word; the default is to interpret speech literally (haqiqah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, only men, unless it is a tribal name
C) Only if they are poor
D) Only if the testator explicitly includes them

Key Takeaway
In a bequest, 'Banu Fulan' includes only men by default, but if it is a tribal name, it includes both men and women.
