ترجمہ اور انہیں میں سے یہ ہے جب کہ ذمی نے ایسی چیز کی وصیت کی جو ہمارے حق میں اور ان کے حق میں قربت ہے جیسے جب کہ وہ بیت المقدس میں چراغ جلانے کی وصیت کرے یا ترک یعنی روم سے جنگ کی وصیت کرے اور یہ جائز ہے خواہ قوم معین ہو یا غیر معین ہو اس لئے کہ یہ اس چیز کی وصیت ہے جو کہ حقیقیہ قربت ہے اور ان کے اعتقاد میں بھی ( قربت ہے)۔ تشریح یہ اقسام اربعہ مذکورہ میں سے تیسری قسم ہے جو ہمارے نزدیک بھی قربت ہو اور ان کے نزدیک بھی قربت ہو تو یہ وصیت بالا تفاق صحیح ہے۔ مثلاً اس نے یہ وصیت کی کہ میرے مال میں سے بیت المقدس میں چراغ جلا دینا یا میرے مال میں سے ترک یعنی روم کی جنگ میں خرچ کرنا ، پھر یہاں قوم کے محصور اور غیر محصور ہونے سے کوئی بحث نہیں۔
Third category. And among them [is the case] when he wills for something that is a qurbah for us and for them, such as when he wills to light lamps in Bayt al-Maqdis or to wage war against the Turks (i.e., the Romans). This is valid, whether the people are specified individuals or not, because it is a will for something that is truly a qurbah, and in their belief as well. Translation: Among these is when a dhimmi wills for something that is a qurbah for us and for them, like when he wills to light lamps in Bayt al-Maqdis or to wage war against the Turks, i.e., the Romans. This is valid, whether the people are specified or not, because it is a will for something that is truly a qurbah and also in their belief. Commentary: This is the third of the four mentioned categories; that which is a qurbah for us and also a qurbah for them, so this will is unanimously valid. For example, he wills that lamps be lit in Bayt al-Maqdis from his wealth, or that it be spent on war against the Turks (Romans). In this case, there is no discussion about the group being confined or not.

Commentary
This passage covers the third category of a dhimmi's will according to the classification in the commentary on al-Hidayah. The testator bequeaths for an act that is considered a qurbah (act of worship) in both Islam and his own religion. Examples given include lighting lamps in Bayt al-Maqdis (which is a place of worship for Muslims and, to some extent, for Christians) or spending on military campaigns against the Turks/Romans (which are enemies of both Muslims and the dhimmi's own state). In this case, the will is valid (jayeaz) regardless of whether the beneficiaries are specified or not. The reason is that the act itself is genuinely a qurbah in both faiths, so the will is inherently meritorious and does not depend on the identity of the recipients. The text explicitly notes that there is no need to discuss confinement (mahsur or ghayr mahsur) here; the will is valid by consensus (bil ittifaq).

Key Terms
قربت حقیقیہ (qurbat haqīqiyyah): An act that is objectively considered worship or drawing near to God in both Islam and the testator's religion.
بیت المقدس (Bayt al-Maqdis): Jerusalem; a holy site for both Muslims and Christians.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's will for an act that is qurbah in both Islam and the testator's religion is valid by consensus, regardless of beneficiary specification, because the act itself is a true qurbah.

Dhimmi's Will for Sinful Acts: When It Is Valid
Ruling on a dhimmi's bequest for sinful purposes with an exception for specified individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing between invalid and valid cases of a dhimmi's will for sinful acts, based on whether beneficiaries are specified.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's bequest for a sinful act is invalid unless the recipients are named individuals — then it is valid as a transfer of ownership.

This lesson examines the fourth category of dhimmi wills: bequests for acts that are sinful in both Islam and the testator's own religion. The Hanafi school rules that such wills are generally invalid, but an important exception exists when the testator names specific beneficiaries. Understanding this exception requires distinguishing between two legal bases for a will: religious merit (qurbah) and property transfer (tamlik).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine what the testator is bequeathing. In this case, it is for acts like female singers and mourners — considered sinful (ma'siyah) in both religions.
The act itself is not a qurbah for either faith.
2
Assess the Beneficiary Description
Check whether the beneficiaries are described generally (e.g., 'female singers') or specified individually (e.g., 'Fatima the singer and Zaynab the mourner').
General description = ghayr mahsur (non-confined); specific = mahsur (confined).
3
Apply the General Rule
If beneficiaries are unspecified, the will is invalid (batil) because it cannot be considered qurbah (sinful act) nor tamlik (ownership transfer requires known recipients).
Unspecified beneficiaries are legally unknown (majhul).
4
Apply the Exception
If beneficiaries are specified individuals, the will is valid as tamlik (transfer of ownership) and istikhlaf (succession), even though the purpose remains sinful.
The validity is based on property law, not religious merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھی قسم
و منها اذا اوصى بما لا يكون قربة لا فى حقنا ولا فى حقهم كما اذا اوصى للمغنيات والنائحات فان هذا غير جائز لانه معصية في حقنا و في حقهم الا ان يكون لقوم باعيانهم فيصح تمليكا و استخلافاً
ترجمہ اور انہیں میں سے ہے جب کہ ذمی ایسی چیز کی وصیت کرے جو نہ ہمارے حق میں قربت ہو اور نہ ان کے حق میں جیسے جب کہ وہ گانے والی عورتوں اور نوحہ کرنے والی عورتوں کے لئے وصیت کرے پس یہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ہمارے اور ان کے حق میں معصیت ہے مگر یہ کہ یہ وصیت کسی معین قوم کے لئے ہو پس صحیح ہے تملیک اور استخلاف کے اعتبار سے ۔ تشریح یہ اقسام اربعہ میں سے چوتھی قسم کی وصیت ہے جو کسی کے نزدیک قربت نہ ہو اس کی وصیت کرے یعنی نہ ان کے نزدیک وہ قربت ہے اور نہ ہمارے نزدیک جیسے وہ وصیت کرے کہ میرا اتنا مال گانے والی ڈومینوں اور نوحہ کرنے والی عورتوں کو دے دینا تو یہ وصیت باطل ہے اس لئے کہ بطور قربت کے اس کو صحیح قرار دیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور نہ بطور تملیک کے اس لئے کہ وہ لوگ غیر محصور ہونے کہ وجہ سے مجہول ہیں اور مجہول کو مالک بنا نا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر کسی معین و محصور قوم کے لئے وصیت کی فلاں فلاں ڈومنی اور فلاں فلاں توجہ کرنے والی عورت تو اب وصیت درست ہے۔ لیکن قربت کی حیثیت سے نہیں بلکہ تملیک اور استخلاف کی حیثیت ہے۔
Fourth category. And among them is when he wills for something that is not a qurbah for us nor for them, such as when he wills for female singers and mourners. So this is not valid because it is a sin (ma'siyah) for us and for them, except if it is for a specified group of individuals, then it is valid as tamlik (transfer of ownership) and istikhlaf (succession). Translation: Among these is when a dhimmi wills for something that is not a qurbah for us nor for them, like when he wills for female singers and mourners. This is not valid because it is a sin for us and for them, unless it is for a specified group of individuals, then it is valid from the perspective of tamlik and istikhlaf. Commentary: This is the fourth of the four categories, a will for something that is not a qurbah in anyone's view. For example, he wills to give his wealth to female singers and mourners. This will is batil (invalid) because it cannot be considered as qurbah, nor as tamlik since those people are unknown (majhul) due to being non-confined (ghayr mahsur). However, if he wills for specified confined individuals, like particular named singers and mourners, then the will is valid, but not as qurbah—rather as tamlik and istikhlaf.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth and final category of a dhimmi's will. Here, the testator bequeaths for something that is not a qurbah in either Islam or his own religion; it is actually a sin (ma'siyah) in both. Examples include bequests to female singers (mughanniyat) and professional mourners (na'ihat) — both professions considered sinful in Islamic law and also likely condemned in the dhimmi's religion. The ruling is that such a will is not valid (ghayr jayeaz) because it is a sin. However, an exception is made if the testator specifies particular individuals (qawm bi a'yanihim). In that case, the bequest is valid, but not as a religiously meritorious act (qurbah) — rather, it is valid as a transfer of ownership (tamlik) and succession (istikhlaf). The reason the general bequest is invalid is twofold: first, it cannot be justified as a qurbah; second, it cannot be considered a tamlik because the beneficiaries are unspecified (ghayr mahsur) and thus unknown (majhul), and ownership cannot be transferred to unknown persons.

Key Terms
معصیت (ma'siyah): An act that is sinful; disobedience to God.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; making someone the owner of property.
استخلاف (istikhlāf): Succession; making someone a successor or trustee over property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dhimmi wills his wealth to be given to 'female singers' without naming any individuals. According to the Hanafi school, this will is:
A) Valid as a charitable act.
B) Valid because singers can own property.
C) Invalid because the beneficiaries are unknown.
D) Invalid only if the testator is Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's will for a sinful purpose is valid only when the beneficiaries are specified individuals, because it then functions as a transfer of ownership (tamlik).

Ruling on the Will of a Bid'ati: Innovator and Apostate in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on will of a bid'ati depending on bid'ah reaching kufr or not; intra-Hanafi dispute on murtadd's transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between bid'ah that constitutes kufr and that which does not, state the ruling on the will in each case, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the apostate's transactions.

Core Idea
Validity of an innovator's will depends on whether bid'ah reaches kufr; if it does, the apostate dispute applies.

This lesson examines how Hanafi fiqh classifies a person of bid'ah (innovation) regarding wills. It distinguishes based on whether the innovation reaches kufr or not, applying the principle of building rulings on the apparent (zahir). It also delves into the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) concerning the validity of an apostate's transactions, particularly for a male versus female apostate.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the bid'ah
Determine whether the person's bid'ah is considered kufr or not. This classification is the key to the ruling.
The text assumes a theological determination of bid'ah reaching kufr.
2
Apply the principle of zahir for non-kufr bid'ah
If the bid'ah does not reach kufr, the person is treated like a Muslim in wills because rulings are based on their apparent state (zahir).
This is an application of the usul principle that legal rulings follow the apparent.
3
Identify the apostate ruling for kufr bid'ah
If the bid'ah reaches kufr, the person is treated as a murtadd (apostate). The validity of his will then follows the known dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that an apostate's transactions (including wills) are suspended (mawquf) until he returns to Islam or is executed. The Sahibayn hold they are valid (ja'iz) in the interim.
The dispute is grounded in differing views on property rights during the state of apostasy.
5
Distinguish the female apostate
For a female apostate (murtaddah), the more correct view (al-asahh) is that her wills are valid because she remains in apostasy (imprisoned, not killed), unlike the male who is killed or converts.
The text explicitly says 'al-asahh' for the murtaddah, indicating tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و صاحب الهوى ان كان لا يكفر فهو فى حق الوصية بمنزلة المسلمين لأنا امرنا ببناء الاحكام على الظاهر وان كان يكفر فهو بمنزلة المرتد فيكون على الخلاف المعروف فى تصرفاته بين ابي حنيفة و صاحبيه و فى المرتدة الاصح انه تصح وصاياها لانها تبقى على الردة بخلاف المرتدلانه يقتل او يسلم
ترجمہ اور صاحب بدعت اگر اس کی تکفیر نہ ہو تو وہ وصیت کے حق میں مسلمانوں کے درجہ میں ہے اس لئے کہ ہم کو ظاہر پر احکام کے مبنی کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور اگر اس کی تکفیر کی جائے تو وہ مرتد کے درجہ میں ہے تو ہو گا اس اختلاف کے مطابق جو معروف ومشہور ہے مرتد کے تصرفات کے سلسلہ میں ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کے درمیان اور مرتدہ میں اسح یہ ہے کہ اس کی وصایا صحیح ہیں اس لئے کہ مرتد ہ ردت پر برقرار رہ سکتی ہے بخلاف مرتد کے اس لئے کہ اس کو قتل کیا جائے گا یا وہ مسلمان ہو گا۔
تشریح یہ ڈمیوں کا بیان چل رہا تھا اسی میں مصنف نے مسلمانوں سے ان لوگوں کا حکم بیان فرمایا جو صاحب ہوئی و بدعت ہیں تو یہاں سے ان کا حکم بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ان کی بدعت حد کفر تک پہنچی ہوئی ہو تو وہ مرتد کے حکم میں ہیں اور اگر حد کفر تک پہنچی ہوئی نہ ہو تو وہ مسلمانوں کے حکم میں ہیں۔ اور مرتد کے بارے میں ہدایہ جلد ثانی کے آخر میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف گذر چکا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مرتد کے تصرفات موقوف ہوں گے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہوں گے۔ اور اگر وصیت کرنے والی مرندہ ہو تو چونکہ اس کو قتل نہیں کیا جا تا بلکہ قید رکھی جائے گی جب تک کہ مسلمان نہ ہو جائے تو مرتد ہ ذمیہ کے درجہ میں ہے اور ڈمیہ کے مثل مرتدہ کے تصرفات نافذ ہوں گے۔ اور مرتد کوقتل کیا جائے گا یا وہ مسلمان ہو جائے تو وہ اپنی روت پر باقی نہیں رہ سکتا اس لئے مرتد ذمی کے درجہ میں نہ ہوگا۔
And the person of bid'ah (innovation): if his innovation is not kufr (disbelief), then with respect to the will he is like a Muslim, because we are commanded to base rulings on the apparent (zahir). And if his innovation is kufr, then he is like an apostate (murtadd), and then it follows the known disagreement regarding the transactions of the murtadd between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Concerning a female apostate (murtaddah), the more correct view is that her wills are valid because she remains in apostasy (she is not killed), unlike the male apostate because he is killed or he becomes Muslim. Translation: And the person of bid'ah: if his innovation does not reach kufr, then in the matter of wills he is in the rank of Muslims because we are commanded to base rulings on the apparent. And if his innovation does reach kufr, then he is in the rank of an apostate. Then it follows the well-known disagreement regarding the transactions of the apostate between Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And for the female apostate, the more correct view is that her wills are valid because she remains in apostasy (i.e., she is not killed but imprisoned), unlike the male apostate because he is killed or he becomes Muslim. Commentary: This follows the discussion on dhimmis. The author now explains the ruling for those among Muslims who are followers of bid'ah. If their bid'ah reaches the level of kufr, they are in the ruling of apostates; if not, they are in the ruling of Muslims. Concerning the apostate, a known disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) has already been mentioned in volume 2 of al-Hidayah: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the transactions of a murtadd are suspended (mawquf), while according to the Sahibayn, they are valid (ja'iz). And if the one making the will is a female apostate, since she is not killed but rather imprisoned until she returns to Islam, she is like a dhimmiyah, and her transactions are effective. Whereas the male apostate is either killed or becomes Muslim, so he does not remain in apostasy, thus he is not like a dhimmi.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the will of a person who is a follower of bid'ah (religious innovation), distinguishing between two cases. First, if the innovation does not constitute kufr (disbelief) according to Islamic theology, the person is treated as a Muslim in matters of wills. This is based on the principle that legal rulings are built on the apparent (zahir) state of a person. Second, if the innovation is deemed kufr, then the person is classified as a murtadd (apostate) and the rules of apostasy apply. Here, the text references a known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) concerning the validity of an apostate's transactions. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the transactions of a murtadd are suspended (mawquf) until he returns to Islam or is executed, while the Sahibayn hold them to be valid (ja'iz). The text then discusses the special case of a female apostate (murtaddah): the more correct (asahh) view is that her wills are valid because she is not executed but rather imprisoned indefinitely until she repents, so she remains in a state of apostasy and thus her transactions are effective, similar to a dhimmiyah. This contrasts with a male apostate who is either killed or readily returns to Islam, so his transactions are not considered continuing.

Key Terms
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religious matters; a belief or practice not found in the original sources.
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate; a Muslim who renounces Islam.
موقوف (mawqūf): Suspended; pending a final determination (e.g., the apostate's acceptance of Islam or execution).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person's bid'ah does not reach the level of kufr, what is the ruling on his will?
A) His will is invalid because he is an innovator.
B) His will is valid and he is treated like a Muslim in this regard.
C) His will is valid only if he repents.
D) His will is suspended pending his return to Islam.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bid'ati's will depends on whether the innovation reaches kufr; if it does, the apostate dispute applies, with the female apostate's will being more clearly valid.

Harbi Musta'min's Will for All Wealth
Ruling on a harbi musta'min's bequest of all property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a harbi musta'min's will for all his property and explain the legal basis using the Hanafi principle of 'illah (effective cause).

Core Idea
A harbi musta'min's will for all his property is valid because his heirs in dar al-harb have no protected rights.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a harbi (a non-Muslim from dar al-harb) who enters dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) and bequeaths all his wealth to a Muslim or a dhimmi. The normal restriction of a will to one-third of the estate is based on protecting heirs' rights, but since the harbi's heirs are in dar al-harb and have no recognized rights, the restriction does not apply. This ruling illustrates how Hanafi fiqh applies causal reasoning (ta'lil) to determine legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
What is the act under discussion? Who is the actor? What is the ruling (valid or invalid)?
The act is a bequest of all property by a harbi musta'min.
2
Recall the general rule for wills
What is the normal limit on bequests in Islamic law? Why does this limit exist?
The general rule is that a will cannot exceed one-third of the estate unless heirs permit, to protect their rights.
3
Trace the dalil (proof)
What is the basis for the exception in this case? Identify the 'illah (effective cause) of the general rule and why it is absent here.
The 'illah is the existence of heirs with protected rights. Here, the harbi's heirs are in dar al-harb and have no such rights.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
Is this ruling agreed upon by all schools? If not, what is the opposing view?
The Hanafi position is that the whole will is valid; some other schools may apply the one-third limit universally.
5
Apply the ruling
Think of a scenario: If the harbi musta'min had heirs in dar al-Islam, would the ruling change? Why?
If the heirs were in dar al-Islam and protected, the one-third limit would apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا دخل الحربى دارنا بامان فاوصى لمسلم او ذمی بماله كله جاز لان امتناع الوصية بما زاد على الثلث لحق الورثة ولهذا ينفذ باجازتهم و ليس لورثته حق مرعى لكونهم فى دار الحرب اذهم اموات في حقنا ولان حرمة ماله باعتبار الامان والامان كان لحقه لالـحـق ورثته
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جب حربی ہمارے دار ( دار الاسلام ) میں امان لے کر داخل ہوا پس اس نے کسی مسلمان یا ڈمی کو اپنے کل مال کی وصیت کر دی تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ ثلاث سے زیادہ کی وصیت کا ممتنع ہونا ور ثا کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اس وجہ سے ورثا کی اجازت سے وہ نافذ ہو جاتی ہے ( یعنی ٹکٹ سے زیادہ کی وصیت ) اور حربی مستامن کے ورثہ کیلئے کوئی ایسا حق نہیں جس کی رعایت کی جائے ورثا کے حق کی وجہ سے ثلاث سے زیادہ کی وصیت ممتنع ہوتی ہے اور حربی مستامن کے ورثاء کا حق ہمارے نزدیک محفوظ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ دارالحرب میں ہیں اور وہ ہمارے حق میں مردوں کی طرح ہیں
He (Imam Muhammad) said: If a harbi enters our abode (dar al-Islam) with aman (safe conduct) and wills all his property to a Muslim or a dhimmi, it is valid. Because the prohibition of a will exceeding one-third is due to the right of the heirs, and thus it is effective with their permission. And there is no right of his heirs that is observed, because they are in dar al-harb, and they are like dead people in our regard. And because the sanctity of his wealth is based on aman, and the aman was for his own right, not for the right of his heirs. Translation: Muhammad said: When a harbi enters our abode (dar al-Islam) with aman and makes a will for a Muslim or a dhimmi of all his wealth, it is valid. Because the restriction of a will exceeding one-third is due to the right of the heirs, and thus it becomes effective with their permission. And the harbi musta'min's heirs have no right that is observed, because they are in dar al-harb, and they are like dead people in our regard. And because the sanctity of his wealth is based on the aman, and the aman was for his own right, not for the right of his heirs. Commentary: The text states that a harbi (a non-Muslim from dar al-harb) who enters dar al-Islam under a guarantee of safety (aman) may make a will for all his property in favor of a Muslim or a dhimmi, and this is valid (ja'iz). The reason given is that the general rule limiting bequests to one-third of the estate is for the protection of the heirs' rights. However, in this case, the harbi's heirs are in dar al-harb and have no protected rights under Islamic law; they are considered legally 'dead' (amwat) from our perspective. Moreover, the inviolability (hurmah) of his property arises solely from the aman grant, which was for his own benefit, not for his heirs' benefit. Therefore, the limitation of one-third does not apply, and the entire bequest is valid.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage, from the sayings of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (قال), provides a specific ruling for a harbi (combatant non-Muslim) who enters dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman). If such a person makes a will bequeathing all his wealth to a Muslim or a dhimmi, the bequest is valid (ja'iz) for all of it. The reasoning is twofold: First, the general principle that a will for more than one-third of the estate is restricted (mumtani') only applies when there are heirs whose rights are protected. Second, the heirs of this harbi musta'min are in dar al-harb and, from the perspective of Islamic law, have no recognized rights; they are like dead people (amwat) in our regard. Additionally, the respect for his property (hurmah) is granted by the aman, which is solely for his own benefit, not his heirs. Therefore, the normal third limitation does not apply, and the entire estate can be willed. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that the rights of the testator's heirs in dar al-harb are not considered in dar al-Islam.

Key Terms
حربی (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim who is from dar al-harb (the abode of war) and has no treaty of protection.
مستأمن (musta'min): A harbi who enters dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman), granting him temporary protection.
امان (amān): Safe conduct or guarantee of security granted to a harbi entering Muslim territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he is not a Muslim and is not bound by Islamic law.
B) Because his heirs in dar al-harb have no protected rights in dar al-Islam.
C) Because the aman allows him to do whatever he wants with his property.
D) Because his heirs have waived their rights.

Key Takeaway
A harbi musta'min's will for all his property is valid because his heirs in dar al-harb have no protected rights, demonstrating the Hanafi method of reasoning based on effective cause ('illah).

Harbi Musta'min's Bequest of All Wealth
Ruling with rational proof on a musta'min's bequest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a harbi musta'min may bequeath all his wealth and explain the Hanafi rationale based on the status of his heirs and the nature of aman.

Core Idea
A harbi musta'min can bequeath all his wealth because his harbi heirs are legally dead and the aman protects his right alone.

In Hanafi fiqh, a non-Muslim who enters Dar al-Islam with temporary safe conduct (amān) is called a musta'min. While Muslim testators are limited to bequeathing one-third of their wealth, this lesson explores a unique ruling: a harbi musta'min may bequeath all his property to a Muslim or dhimmi. Why does the one-third rule not apply? The answer lies in the legal status of his heirs and the nature of the inviolability of his wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a musta'min bequeathing all his wealth to a Muslim or dhimmi. The ruling is that it is permissible (jāʾiz) and the bequest is valid (sahīḥ).
The ruling directly contradicts the usual one-third limitation for Muslims.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The text provides a rational proof: harbi heirs are like dead in our right, so they have no claim. Also, the inviolability of the musta'min's wealth stems from the aman granted to him personally.
The proof is aqlī (rational) rather than naqlī (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The legal link: the musta'min's heirs are harbis in Dār al-Ḥarb, hence legally nonexistent for inheritance purposes. The amān creates a right only for the musta'min, not his heirs. Thus, no third-party right prevents him from bequeathing all.
This reasoning is an application of the Ḥanafī principle that harbīs have no protected rights in Dār al-Islam.
4
Address the objection
The imagined objection: 'How can he ignore the heirs' rights?' The answer restates the grounds: harbī heirs are unworthy of consideration, and the amān is the musta'min's right.
The Ḥanafī position is clear and consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دار الحرب میں ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لئے حربین ہمارے حق میں مردے ہیں اور اس لئے کہ مستامن کے مال کی حرمت امان کے اعتبار سے ہے اور امان مستامن کا حق ہے نہ کہ مستامن کے ورثا کا حق۔ تشریح کوئی کا فر حربی امان لے کر ہمارے دار الاسلام میں آیا اور یہاں اس نے کسی مسلمان یا کسی ذمی کو اپنے پورے مال کی وصیت کر دی تو یہ جائز ہے، شاید اس پر یہ اشکال ہو کہ یہ کیسے جائز ہوا جب کہ اس کے دو ٹکٹ کے اندر ورثا کا حق ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں تو ور شاوہ حربی ہیں جو دار الحزب میں ہیں اور وہ اس قابل نہیں ہیں کہ ان کے حق کی رعایت ہو اس لئے کہ وہ تو ہمارے حق میں مردوں کے مثل ہیں ۔ اور یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ مستامن کے مال میں جو حرمت پیدا ہوئی ہے کہ اس سے تعرض نہ کیا جائے یہ حق مستامن کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ حق در حالی وجہ ہے۔
Because of being in Dar al-Harb, therefore the harbis are like dead in our right, and because the inviolability of the musta'min's wealth is based on the aman, and the aman is the right of the musta'min, not the right of the musta'min's heirs. Elaboration: A harbi infidel came to our Dar al-Islam with aman, and here he bequeathed all his wealth to a Muslim or a dhimmi; this is permissible. Perhaps an objection arises: how is this permissible when in his [Islamic] law the heirs have a right? The answer is that here the heirs are harbis who are in Dar al-Harb, and they are not worthy of consideration because they are like dead in our right. And there is also the reason that the inviolability that has arisen in the musta'min's wealth (that it should not be interfered with) is due to the musta'min's right, not due to the heirs' right.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a harbi musta'min can bequeath all his wealth to a Muslim or dhimmi in Dar al-Islam. The author first gives the legal rationale: harbi heirs are considered like dead in the view of Islamic law because they are in Dar al-Harb and have no protection. Therefore, their potential inheritance rights are not considered. Additionally, the sanctity of the musta'min's wealth is derived from the aman (safe conduct) granted to him personally, not to his heirs. Hence, he has full disposal over his wealth, including bequeathing all of it. The commentary then addresses a possible objection: how can he ignore the heirs' rights? The answer reiterates that harbi heirs are not entitled to consideration in Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms
مستامن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters Dar al-Islam with temporary safe conduct (aman).
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a covenant and is in a state of war with Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a harbi musta'min allowed to bequeath all his wealth to a Muslim or dhimmi?
A) Because he is a Muslim
B) Because his harbi heirs are considered like dead in our right
C) Because he has no heirs
D) Because the one-third rule does not apply to non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
A harbī musta'min can bequeath all his wealth because his harbī heirs have no protected rights, and the inviolability of his wealth is his personal right from the amān.

Ruling on a Harbi Musta'min's Partial Bequest
States ruling on musta'min bequeathing less than all, remainder to heirs based on his right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a harbi musta'min's bequest of less than all wealth and explain that the remainder returns to his heirs based on his own right.

Core Idea
A musta'min's partial bequest is valid; the rest goes to his heirs as a matter of his own right, not theirs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a harbi musta'min (a non-Muslim from enemy territory with safe passage) who bequeaths less than his entire wealth while in Muslim territory. The matn clarifies that the bequest is taken and the remaining property is returned to his heirs—not because the heirs have a right to it, but out of respect for the musta'min's own right to have his estate disposed according to his intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
The parties are a harbi musta'min (the testator) and his harbi heirs. The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of less than all his wealth.
2
State the ruling on the bequest
The bequest itself is taken (i.e., valid and executed). This means the musta'min's disposal of that portion is effective under Islamic law.
The ruling does not mention any limit like one-third, which applies to Muslims.
3
Determine the fate of the remainder
The remaining wealth (the part not bequeathed) is returned to his harbi heirs.
4
Understand the legal basis
The remainder returns to the heirs not because they have a right (since harbis have no inheritance rights under Islamic law), but because it stems from the musta'min's own right: he did not dispose of that part, so it goes to his natural heirs out of respect for his intention.
This is a rational (aqli) consideration, not a text-based inheritance rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان اوصى باقل من ذالك اخذت الوصية و يرد الباقى على ورثته و ذالك من حق المستامن ايضاً
And if he bequeathed less than that, the bequest is taken and the rest is returned to his heirs, and that is also from the right of the musta'min.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This matn states the ruling: if a harbi musta'min bequeaths less than all his wealth, the bequest is executed to the extent of the bequeathed amount, and the remaining wealth is returned to his harbi heirs. However, this is not because the heirs have a right to the remainder, but rather out of consideration for the musta'min himself: since he did not dispose of it, it should go to his natural heirs as a matter of his own right (i.e., his intention). The commentary explains that the return is not out of respect for the heirs' right (since they are harbis and not entitled), but out of respect for the musta'min's right that his remaining property should go to his rightful heirs according to his own law.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim from enemy territory (harbi) who has been granted safe passage (aman) into Muslim territory for a temporary period.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under the protection of an Islamic state (i.e., from dar al-harb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, why is the remainder of a musta'min's wealth (after a partial bequest) returned to his heirs?
A) Because the heirs have a legal right to inherit from him
B) Because it is out of respect for the musta'min's own right
C) Because the one-third limit forces the rest to go to heirs
D) Because the bequest is invalid, so all goes to heirs

Key Takeaway
A harbi musta'min's partial bequest is valid, and the unbequeathed remainder returns to his heirs by virtue of his own right, not theirs.

Ruling on Musta'min's Manumission and Tadbir at Death
States that a musta'min's freeing of slave or tadbir at death is valid without one-third limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a musta'min's freeing of a slave or tadbir at death is valid without the one-third limit and explain the rationale based on the lack of heirs' rights.

Core Idea
A musta'min's deathbed manumission is unrestricted by the one-third limit because his harbi heirs have no claim.

In this lesson, we examine a specific extension of the principle that a musta'min's dispositions at death are not constrained by the one-third rule that applies to Muslims. The passage from Al-Hidayah states that both manumission (itq) and tadbir (freeing upon death) are fully valid and not subject to the one-third limit. The reason is the same as previously established: the musta'min's enemy heirs have no legal right to restrict his actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the actor
The actor is a harbi musta'min (a non-Muslim granted safe passage into Dar al-Islam). The acts are freeing a slave at death (itq fima yamlik) and making a tadbir contract.
Note the word 'mudabbar' meaning a slave freed upon the master's death.
2
State the ruling
Both acts are valid (sahih) and effective from the musta'min, meaning the slave becomes free.
3
Identify the exception to the general rule
For Muslims, bequests (including manumission) are limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent. Here, no such limit applies.
The text explicitly says 'without consideration of the third'.
4
Explain the rationale (dalil)
The text says 'because of what we have explained' – referring to the earlier principle that the musta'min's harbi heirs are like dead (i.e., have no right to inherit), so there is no one to restrict him.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the absence of heirs' rights.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may apply the one-third rule uniformly to all testators, including musta'mins.
The Hanafi position is specific to the status of harbi heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اعتق عبده عند الموت او دبر عبده في دار الاسلام فذالك صحيح منه من غير اعتبار الثلث لما بينا
And if he freed his slave at death or made his slave a mudabbar in Dar al-Islam, that is valid from him without consideration of the third, because of what we have explained.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This matn extends the same principle to manumission and tadbir (a contract where the slave is freed upon the master's death). If a harbi musta'min frees his slave at the time of death or makes a tadbir contract in Dar al-Islam, it is fully valid and not restricted to the one-third limit that applies to Muslims. The reason is the same: his harbi heirs do not have any right that would restrict his disposition. Therefore, the entire slave is freed, even if it exceeds one-third of the estate.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is contractually freed upon the master's death.
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim (harbi) who is granted temporary safe passage (aman) into Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a musta'min's freeing of a slave at death valid without considering the one-third limit?
A) Because the one-third rule only applies to Muslims
B) Because his harbi heirs have no right that would restrict him
C) Because the slave is also a musta'min
D) Because the freeing was done in Dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
A musta'min's deathbed manumission and tadbir in Dar al-Islam are fully valid and not subject to the one-third limit because his harbi heirs have no legal right to inherit or restrict his disposal of property.

Bequest to a Harbi Musta'min: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest to a musta'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on a bequest to a harbi musta'min, explain each dalil, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A musta'min's transactional capacity in Dar al-Islam is disputed: like a dhimmi (Muhammad) or tied to temporary stay (Shaykhayn).

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a Muslim or dhimmi can bequeath property to a harbi musta'min in Dar al-Islam. The disagreement centers on the legal status of the musta'min: does he enjoy the same capacity as a dhimmi for lifetime transactions, thereby extending to bequests? Or does his temporary status and intention to return to Dar al-Harb prevent such a bequest? By the end, you will understand both proofs and the practical consequence of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the dispute
Identify the ruling: a Muslim or dhimmi making a bequest to a harbi musta'min. Note that the Hanafi school has two positions.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
2
Outline Imam Muhammad's position and his qiyas
Imam Muhammad holds it permissible. He analogizes the musta'min to a dhimmi while in Dar al-Islam. Since a dhimmi can receive bequests, so can a musta'min.
The qiyas is based on the illa of being in Dar al-Islam with transactional capacity.
3
Outline the Shaykhayn's position and their counter-argument
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it impermissible. They argue that the musta'min is from ahl al-harb, intends to return, and cannot stay indefinitely without jizya, so his status is not permanent like a dhimmi's.
Their dalil emphasizes the temporary nature of the musta'min's stay.
4
Compare the two views and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether the bequest is executed or void. According to Imam Muhammad, the bequest is valid and must be given; according to the Shaykhayn, it is invalid and the property remains in the estate.
This affects the executor and heirs.
5
Assess which view is preferred in the madhhab
The text does not explicitly state tarjih, but later Hanafi practice often relies on Imam Muhammad's view as recorded in zahir al-riwayah.
However, the view of the Shaykhayn remains part of the madhhab and may be followed in some contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کذالک لو اوصى له مسلم او ذمى بوصية جاز لانه مادام فى دار الاسلام فهو فى المعاملات بمنزلة الذمى ولهذا تصح عقود التمليكات منه في حال حياته و يصح تبرعه في حياته فكذا بعد مماته۔ وعن ابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف انه لا يجوز لانه مستامن من اهل الحرب اذ هو على قصد الرجوع و يمكن منه ولا يمكن من زيادة المقام على السنة الا بالجزية
And likewise, if a Muslim or a dhimmi made a bequest to him, it is permissible, because as long as he is in Dar al-Islam, he is in transactions like a dhimmi, and therefore the contracts of ownership from him are valid during his lifetime, and his gift is valid during his lifetime, so likewise after his death. And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible, because he is a musta'min from the people of war, since he intends to return, and he is enabled to do so, and he cannot increase his stay beyond a year except with jizya.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a Muslim or dhimmi can make a bequest to a harbi musta'min. Imam Muhammad's position is that it is permissible. He analogizes the musta'min to a dhimmi while he is in Dar al-Islam: just as contracts and gifts (tabarru') from a Muslim to a dhimmi are valid during the Muslim's lifetime, so too a bequest (which is a posthumous gift) is valid. The basis is that the musta'min's legal capacity in transactions is the same as a dhimmi's. On the other hand, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that it is not permissible. Their reasoning: the musta'min is from the people of war (ahl al-harb) because he intends to return to Dar al-Harb. He is allowed to leave at any time and cannot stay more than a year without paying jizya (which would make him a dhimmi). Therefore, his status is not permanent like a dhimmi's, and bequests to him are not valid because there is no lasting bond of protection. The commentary explains that the dispute hinges on whether the musta'min is treated like a dhimmi in all transactional matters or not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is often Imam Muhammad's view, but the text does not explicitly state tarjih.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living permanently under Muslim protection with a covenant (dhimma).
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters Dar al-Islam temporarily under a safe conduct (aman).
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war (harb) with Muslims, not under a covenant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is a bequest to a musta'min valid?
A) The musta'min is a Muslim.
B) The musta'min is like a dhimmi in transactions while in Dar al-Islam.
C) The musta'min has paid jizya.
D) The bequest is from a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest to a harbi musta'min is disputed within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad analogizes him to a dhimmi, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf emphasize his temporary status.

Dhimmi's Bequests: Limits and Permissibility
States rulings for a dhimmi's bequests: more than one-third, to an heir, to different milla, or to a harbi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings regarding a dhimmi's bequests and explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) used for each.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's bequest is limited by Islamic law: more than one-third or to an heir is invalid; between non-Muslims of different creeds it is valid; to a harbi it is invalid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the extent to which a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state) can make bequests. While dhimmis are not required to follow Islamic worship rites, they have committed to Islamic laws in transactional matters. The rulings here are derived by qiyas (analogy) from Muslim inheritance and bequest rules, as well as from inheritance rules among non-Muslims. Let's dissect each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios and their rulings
Read the passage and list each case: (1) bequest >1/3 or to an heir: batil; (2) bequest to different milla: sahih; (3) bequest to harbi: batil.
2
Analyze the analogy for the first ruling
The text says 'by analogy to Muslims' – identify the asl (Muslims' limit of 1/3 and no bequest to heir) and the far' (dhimmi's bequest). The illa is the commitment to Islamic transactional laws.
This is qiyas jaliy.
3
Analyze the analogy for the second ruling
The text says 'by analogy to inheritance' – since all disbelief is one milla for inheritance, bequests between different non-Muslim communities are valid.
What is the asl here? It is inheritance among non-Muslims of different creeds.
4
Analyze the third ruling
Bequest to a harbi in Dar al-Islam is invalid because inheritance is impossible due to different abodes, and bequest is 'its sister' (i.e., follows inheritance rules).
The analogy is to inheritance being prevented by difference of dar.
5
Synthesize the principle
Summarize: A dhimmi's bequest is governed by the same limitations as a Muslim's bequest (1/3 rule, no heir) and also mirrors inheritance rules regarding milla and dar.
The key is that dhimmis accepted Islamic law in transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أوصى الذمى باكثر من الثلث او لبعض ورثته لا يجوز اعتبارا بالمسلمين لانهم التزموا احكام الاسلام فيما يرجع الى المعاملات ولو أوصى لخلاف ملته جاز اعتباراً بالارث اذ الكفر كله ملة واحدة ولو أوصى لحربى فى دار الاسلام لا يجوز لان الارث ممتنع لتباين الدارين والوصية اخته والله أعلم
And if a dhimmi bequeathed more than one-third or to some of his heirs, it is not valid, by analogy to Muslims, because they (dhimmis) have committed to the rulings of Islam regarding transactions. And if he bequeathed to someone of a different milla (religious community), it is valid, by analogy to inheritance, since all disbelief is one milla. And if he bequeathed to a harbi in Dar al-Islam, it is not valid, because inheritance is prevented due to the difference of the two abodes, and bequest is its sister. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage lays out three rulings for a dhimmi's bequests: First, if a dhimmi bequeaths more than one-third of his estate, or bequeaths to some of his heirs (while excluding others), it is not valid. This is by analogy (qiyas) to Muslims, because dhimmis have agreed to abide by Islamic laws in transactional matters, including the law of bequests. Second, if a dhimmi bequeaths to someone of a different non-Muslim religious community (e.g., a Jew bequeaths to a Christian), it is valid. The reasoning is by analogy to inheritance: in inheritance, all non-Muslims are considered one milla (religious community) for the purpose of mutual inheritance, so similarly bequests between them are valid. Third, if a dhimmi bequeaths to a harbi (a non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb) who is in Dar al-Islam, it is not valid. The reason is that inheritance between a dhimmi and a harbi is impossible due to the difference of the two abodes, and bequest is considered similar to inheritance in this respect (اخته i.e., its sister). The commentary explains that the principle is that bequest follows the rules of inheritance in terms of eligibility of the beneficiary.

Key Terms
ملة (milla): Religious community or creed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a dhimmi's bequest to someone of a different non-Muslim religion valid?
A) Because all non-Muslims are equal
B) Because it is analogized to inheritance where all disbelief is one milla
C) Because the bequest is less than one-third
D) Because the beneficiary is a dhimmi

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's bequests are governed by the same limitations as a Muslim's (one-third, no heir) and also mirror inheritance rules regarding milla and dar.

When Does Silence Become Acceptance? Hanafi Ruling on Executorship
Explains when rejection of executorship is valid and when silence becomes acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of acceptance/rejection of executorship and explain the legal distinction between executorship and agency.

Core Idea
An executor cannot reject after the testator's death; silence gives choice, but selling binds.

When a person is appointed executor (wasi) by a dying testator, the acceptance or rejection of that role has specific legal consequences. The Hanafi school distinguishes the executor's situation from that of a mere agent (wakil), because the executor acts after the testator's death, where deception becomes irreversible. This passage from Al-Hidayah lays out the rules: rejection in the testator's presence is valid, silence leaves the executor with a choice, but selling any of the estate's property after death constitutes binding acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The matn mentions three situations: rejection in the testator's presence, silence until death, and selling something from the estate after death.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For rejection in presence: valid. For silence until death: executor has option to accept or reject. For selling after death: executorship becomes binding.
3
Understand the rationale (dalil)
The text uses the absence of deception (ghurur) and the testator's ability to appoint another. Since rejection in presence does not deceive, it is valid; after death, deception would harm the testator who relied on acceptance.
4
Compare with agency (wikalah)
The commentary notes that an agent can reject in the principal's absence because the principal is alive and can act himself. However, if the agency was for a specific slave and the agent buys it for himself, rejection is invalid.
5
Note the practical effect of selling
Selling any part of the estate after death is a clear indication of commitment (iltizam) and acceptance, even if the executor never verbally accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ تشریح زید نے اپنی موت کے قریب خالد کو اپنا وصی بنایا اور خالد نے اس ذمہ داری کو قبول کر لیا یعنی موصی کے سامنے خالد نے قبول کر لیا اور پھر اس کی عدم موجودگی میں وصایت کو رد کر دیا تو وصایت رد نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ زید تو خالد پر اعتماد کرتے ہوئے دنیا سے رخصت ہو چکا ہے تو اگر خالد کا رد معتبر ہو جائے تو اس میں ضرر شدید ہے اور اس میں زید کو دھوکہ دینا ہے اور دھوکہ دینا حرام ہے لہذا زید کا یہ رو مردود ہوگا۔
ہاں اگر زید نے خالد کو وکیل بنایا کہ میرے لئے کوئی غلام خرید و یا وکیل بنایا کہ میرا مال فروخت کر دو اور خالد نے زید کی عدم موجودگی میں وکالت کا انکار کر دیا تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ یہاں کوئی ضرر نہیں کیونکہ زید خود زندہ ہے صاحب قدرت ہے اور اس کام کو خود انجام دے سکتا ہے۔
البتہ اگر زید نے کسی معین غلام کو خریدنے کے لئے خالد کو وکیل بنایا تھا اور خالد نے زید کی عدم موجودگی میں وکالت کو رد کر دیا اور پھر اس غلام کو اپنے لئے خرید لیا تو وکالت رد نہ ہوگی اور یہ غلام زید کے لئے ہوگا۔
اگر وصی وصایت موصی کے سامنے رد کر دے تو رد معتبر ہے
فان ردها فى وجهه فهو رد لانه ليس للموصى ولاية الزامه التصرف ولا غرور فيه لانه يمكنه ان ينيب غيره وان لم يقبل ولم يرد حتى مات الموصى فهو بالخيار ان شاء قبل وان شاء لم يقبل لان الموصى ليس له ولاية الالزام فبقى مخيراً فلوانه باع شيئا من تركته فقد لزمته لان ذالك دلالة الالتزام والقبول وهو معتبر بعد الموت
ترجمہ پس اگر وصی نے وصایت کو موصی کے سامنے رد کر دیا تو رد ہو گیا اس لئے کہ موصی کے وصی پر تصرف کو لازم کرنے کی ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ اس میں کوئی دھوکہ ہے اس لئے کہ موصی کے لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ اس کے غیر کو نائب بنائے اور اگر وصی نے نہ قبول کیا اور نہ رد کیا یہاں تک کہ موصی مرگیا تو وصی کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے قبول کرے اور اگر چاہے تو قبول نہ کرے اس لئے کہ موصی کو الزام کی ولایت نہیں ہے تو وصی مخیر رہا پس اگر وصی نے موصی کے ترکہ میں سے کوئی چیز بیچ دی تو وصایت اس پر لازم ہوگئی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ( بیچنا ) التزام اور قبول کرنے کی دلیل ہے اور قبول کرنا موت کے بعد معتبر ہے۔ تشریح اگر خالد نے زید کے سامنے ہی وصایت کو رد کر دیا تو رد ہو جائے گا کیونکہ زید کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ دوسرے پر اس تصرف کو لازم کر دے یعنی زید کو خالد پر ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ہے۔ اور جب خالد نے زید کے سامنے رد کیا ہے تو اس میں دھوکہ کی بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں زید کسی دوسرے کو اپنا وصی مقرر کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر خالد نے موصی کے کہنے کے بعد نہ قبول کیا اور نہ رد کیا بلکہ خاموش رہا یہاں تک کہ زید کا انتقال ہو گیا تو خالد کو اختیار ہے خواہ قبول کرے خواہ رد کرے اس لئے کہ موصی کو اس پر ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ہے لہذا خالد کو اختیار ہے ہاں اگر اس نے قبول تو نہیں کیا تھا لیکن زید کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ترکہ میں سے کسی چیز کو بیچ دے تو اب یہ وصی بن گیا اور ولایت اس کے لئے لازم ہو گئی اس لئے کہ بیع التزام اور قبول کی علامت ہے اور موت موصی کے بعد قبول و التزام معتبر ہے۔
Book of Wills. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah vol. 16. Explanation: Zaid near his death made Khalid his executor and Khalid accepted this responsibility in the presence of the testator, then rejected the executorship in his absence. The rejection is not valid because Zaid left the world trusting Khalid; if Khalid's rejection were accepted, it would cause severe harm and deception, and deception is haram, so this rejection is rejected. Yes, if Zaid made Khalid an agent to buy a slave for him or to sell his property, and Khalid rejected the agency in Zaid's absence, it is valid because there is no harm—Zaid is alive and capable of doing it himself. However, if Zaid made Khalid an agent to buy a specific slave, and Khalid rejected the agency in Zaid's absence, then bought the slave for himself, the agency is not rejected and the slave is for Zaid. If the executor rejects executorship before the testator, the rejection is valid. (Text) For if he rejected it in his presence, it is a rejection because the testator has no authority to compel him to act, and there is no deception since he can appoint another. And if he neither accepted nor rejected until the testator died, he has the option: if he wishes he accepts, if he wishes he does not accept, because the testator has no authority to compel, so he remains with choice. And if he sold something from his estate, it becomes binding on him because that indicates commitment and acceptance, and acceptance is valid after death. (Translation) So if the executor rejected executorship before the testator, it is rejected because the testator has no authority to compel the executor to act, and there is no deception because the testator can appoint another. And if the executor neither accepted nor rejected until the testator died, he has the option: if he wishes he accepts, if he wishes he does not accept, because the testator has no authority to compel, so the executor remains with choice. Then if the executor sold something from the testator's estate, executorship becomes binding on him because selling indicates commitment and acceptance, and acceptance after death is valid. Explanation: If Khalid rejected executorship before Zaid, it is rejected because Zaid has no authority to compel Khalid to act. And since Khalid rejected in Zaid's presence, there is no deception—Zaid can appoint another. And if Khalid after the testator's statement neither accepted nor rejected but remained silent until Zaid died, Khalid has the option to accept or reject because the testator has no authority to compel. However, if after Zaid's death he sells something from the estate, he becomes executor and authority becomes binding on him because selling indicates commitment and acceptance, and acceptance and commitment after the testator's death are valid.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Wills discusses the rulings on acceptance and rejection of executorship (wasiyah). The opening Urdu sharh clarifies a key distinction: if a person (testator) appoints an executor (wasi) and the executor accepts in the testator's presence but later, after the testator's death, rejects the executorship, that rejection is invalid. Why? Because the testator died trusting him; allowing rejection would cause harm and deception, which is haram. However, in the case of agency (wikalah) for a general task (like buying a slave or selling property), rejection during the principal's absence is valid—there's no deception since the principal is alive and can act himself. But there's an exception: if the agent was appointed to buy a specific slave, rejects the agency in the principal's absence, then buys that slave for himself, the agency is not rejected and the slave belongs to the principal. The Arabic matn then states: rejection in the testator's presence is valid because the testator has no authority to compel the executor to act, and there's no deception since he can appoint another. If the executor neither accepts nor rejects until the testator dies, he retains the choice—he may accept or not. But if he sells something from the estate after death, that act constitutes acceptance and binds him to the executorship. The translation and commentary clarify each point. The Hanafi position is clear: executorship becomes binding only upon express acceptance or implied acceptance through an act like selling. The ruling on selling as acceptance is a key feature: the sale is not just valid but itself becomes evidence of acceptance, even if the executor was unaware of the appointment (as the next lesson will discuss).

Key Terms
وصاية (wasayah): Executorship; the appointment of a person to manage the testator's affairs after death.
وصي (wasi): The executor or trustee appointed to handle the estate after death.
غرور (ghurur): Deception; leading someone to rely on a false belief. Here it refers to the testator relying on the executor's acceptance, which would be betrayed if rejection is allowed after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the executor rejects executorship in the testator's presence?
A) The rejection is valid.
B) The rejection is invalid.
C) The executor must get court approval.
D) The testator can force acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, executorship becomes binding only upon express acceptance or implied acceptance through an act like selling after the testator's death.

The Requirement of Knowledge in Executorship vs Agency
Ruling with proof on executorship vs agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the validity of a sale made by an executor without knowledge, and distinguish it from an agent's sale by identifying the underlying principle of khilafah vs inabah.

Core Idea
Executor succeeds like an heir; agent is a deputy who must know.

This lesson explains a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: why a sale by an executor remains valid even if he was unaware of his appointment, while a sale by an agent in the same situation is void. The difference hinges on whether the representative is a successor (khalifah) or a deputy (na'ib). The proof rests on an analogy to inheritance, which operates automatically without the heir's knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the two rulings: the executor's sale is valid whether or not he knew of his appointment; the agent's sale is invalid if he lacked knowledge.
The ruling applies to any sale of the testator's estate by the executor.
2
Understand the Legal Constructs
Recognise that executorship is khilafah (succession) transferring authority at death, while agency is inabah (delegation) during the principal's lifetime.
Khilafah operates like a caliphate; inabah is mere deputyship.
3
Follow the Proof (Qiyas)
Trace the analogy: the executor is like an heir; just as inheritance transfers ownership without the heir's knowledge, executorship transfers authority without the executor's knowledge.
The analogy is to inheritance (al-ith), which is also a form of khilafah.
4
Apply the Practical Consequence
If an executor sells property before learning of the appointment, the sale binds him and implies acceptance of the executorship. If an agent does the same, the sale is void.
This difference has direct implications in estate administration vs. agency contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
۲۳۶
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۹
التزام اور قبول کی علامت ہے اور موت موصی کے بعد قبول و التزام معتبر ہے۔
بھی موصی کے ترکہ سے کوئی چیز فروخت کر دے تو یہ بیع نافذ ہے یا نہیں
وينفذ البيع لصدوره من الوصى وسواء علم بالوصاية او لم يعلم بخلاف الوكيل اذا لم يعلم بالتوكيل فباع حيث لا ينفذ لان الوصاية خلافة لانه يختص بحال انقطاع ولاية الميت فتنقل الولاية اليه واذا كانت خلافة لا يتوقف على العلم كالوراثة اما التوكيل انابة لثبوته فى حال قيام ولاية المنيب فلا يصح من غير علمه كاثبات الملك بالبيع والشراء وقد بينا طريق العلم و شرط الاخبار فيما تقدم من الكتب
ترجمہ اور بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی بیع کے صادر ہونے کی وجہ سے وصی کی طرف سے اور خواہ وصی کو وصایت کا علم ہو یا نہ ہو بخلاف وکیل کے جب کہ اس کو تو کیل کا علم نہ ہو پس اس نے بیع کی تو نافذ نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ وصایت تو خلافت ہے اس لئے کہ وصایت مختص ہے میت کی ولایت کے انقطاع کے وقت پس ولایت وصی کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گی اور جب کہ وصایت خلافت ہے تو خلافت علم پر موقوف نہیں بے مثل وارث کے بہر حال تو کیل انابت ہے تو کیل کے ثابت ہونے کی وجہ سے منیب کی ولایت کے قائم ہونے کے وقت میں تو توکیل صحیح نہ ہو گی بغیر علم وکیل کے جیسے بیج اور شراء کے ذریعہ ملک کا اثبات۔
اور ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں علم کے طریقہ کو اور اخبار کی شرط کو ان بہت سی کتابوں میں جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہیں۔
تشریح وصی نے جو موصی کے ترکہ میں سے کسی چیز کو فروخت کر دیا ہے تو یہ بیع نافذ ہے یا نہیں؟ ف فر مایا کہ بچی بھی نافذ ہے اور یہ بیچ دلیل قبول بھی ہے اور یہی نہیں بلکہ اگر وصی نے بیچ کی اور اب تک وصی کو یہ بھی علم نہیں ہوا کہ زید نے مجھے وصی بنایا تھا تب بھی بیچ صحیح و نافذ ہے۔ اور اگر زید نے خالد کو وکیل بنایا کہ وہ میرا افلاں سامان فروخت کرے اور خالد کو اس تو کیل کا علم نہیں ہوا اور علم سے پہلے ہی اتفاق سے خالد نے اس سامان کو فروخت کر دیا تو بیع نافذ نہ ہوگی اور وصایت اور توکیل میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ وصایت خلافت ہے اور تو کیل انابت ہے۔
خلافت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ موصی کی موت کے بعد وصی کو تصرف کا اختیار ہو گا اور انابت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مؤکل موجود ہے اور اس کو تصرف پر قدرت حاصل ہے پھر بھی وکیل کو تصرف کا اختیار دیا ہے تو وکیل اپنے موکل کا نائب ہے خلیفہ نہیں ہے۔ حضرات شیخین آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے خلیفہ ہیں اور نائب مہتم مہتمم صاحب کے خلیفہ نہیں بلکہ نائب ہیں۔
جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ وصایت خلافت ہے اور تو کیل اثابت ہے تو اب دونوں کا الگ الگ قانون سنئے۔ خلافت کا قانون یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے ثبوت میں علم کی محتاج نہیں ہے جیسے وراثت چونکہ خلافت ہے وارث کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو وہ وارث ہو گیا اسی طرح وصایت خلافت ہے لہذ اوصی کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو تو وہ وصی ہو گیا۔
اور انابت کا اصول یہ ہے کہ جب تک نائب کو یہ معلوم نہ ہو جائے کہ میں فلاں کا نائب ہوں جب تک نیابت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔ جیسے خالد کے لئے زید نے ایک گھوڑ ا خریدا اور خالد کو اس کا علم نہیں ہے اور اسی حال میں خالد نے اس گھوڑے میں کچھ تصرف کیا تو
Book of Wills. 236. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary of Bidayah vol. 19. And selling something from the testator's estate—is this sale valid? (Text) And the sale is valid because it originates from the executor, whether he knew of the executorship or not, unlike the agent who, if he did not know of the agency and sold, it is not valid. Because executorship is succession (khilafah); it is specific to the time of cessation of the deceased's authority, so authority transfers to him. And when it is succession, it does not depend on knowledge, like inheritance. As for agency, it is delegation (inabah); it is established during the continuing authority of the principal, so it is not valid without his knowledge, like establishing ownership by sale and purchase. And we have explained the method of knowledge and the condition of notification in earlier books. (Translation) And the sale is valid because it originates from the executor, whether he knew of the executorship or not, unlike the agent when he did not know of the agency and sold—it is not valid. Because executorship is succession; it is specific to the time of cessation of the deceased's authority, so authority transfers to the executor. And since it is succession, it does not depend on knowledge, like inheritance. As for agency, it is delegation; it is established during the continuing authority of the principal, so it is not valid without the agent's knowledge, like establishing ownership by sale and purchase. And we have explained the method of knowledge and the condition of notification in many previous books. Explanation: The executor sold something from the testator's estate—is this sale valid? He says that the sale is valid and it is evidence of acceptance. Not only that, but even if the executor sold without knowing that Zaid had appointed him executor, the sale is still valid and effective. However, if Zaid made Khalid his agent to sell a certain item, and Khalid had no knowledge of the agency, and coincidentally sold that item before knowledge, the sale is not valid. The reason for the difference is that executorship is succession, while agency is delegation. Succession means that after the testator's death, the executor has authority to act; delegation means the principal is alive and has the power to act, yet he authorizes the agent—so the agent is a deputy, not a successor. The two Shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar) are the caliphs of the Prophet (peace be upon him), while a deputy (na'ib) of an administrator is not a caliph but a deputy. Now that we know executorship is succession and agency is delegation, hear the distinct rules. The rule of succession is that it does not require knowledge for its establishment, like inheritance: because inheritance is succession, the heir becomes heir whether he knows or not. Similarly, executorship is succession, so the executor becomes executor whether he knows or not. The principle of delegation is that delegation is not established until the deputy knows that he is the deputy of so-and-so. For example, Zaid bought a horse for Khalid and Khalid has no knowledge of it, and in that state Khalid disposed of the horse—
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on executorship but shifts to a critical distinction: the validity of a sale made by an executor who does not know he has been appointed, compared to an agent in the same situation. The matn states clearly: a sale by the executor is valid whether he knew of the executorship or not; but a sale by an agent who did not know of the agency is not valid. The reason is that executorship is khilafah (succession) while agency is inabah (delegation). The commentator explains: executorship is 'specific to the time of cessation of the deceased's authority', meaning at death the testator's authority ends and is transferred to the executor. This transfer is like inheritance—the heir inherits whether he knows or not. Delegation, however, operates while the principal is alive and retains authority; the agent acts as a deputy, and for delegation to be valid, the agent must know he is an agent. The Urdu commentary gives a practical example: if a testator makes someone executor without the person's knowledge, and that person later sells an item from the estate, the sale is valid and even serves as acceptance. But if a principal appoints an agent to sell, and the agent sells without knowing, the sale is null. The commentator uses the example of the Prophet's caliphs (Abu Bakr and Umar) to illustrate khilafah: they were successors, not mere deputies. The underlying principle is that succession (khilafah) transfers authority automatically and does not require the successor's awareness, while delegation (inabah) requires consent based on knowledge. This is a foundational difference in Hanafi fiqh between the two legal constructs.

Key Terms
خلافة (khilafah): Succession; the transfer of authority from the testator to the executor after death, similar to how a caliph succeeds the Prophet.
إِنَابَة (inabah): Delegation; appointing a deputy (na'ib) to act on one's behalf while the principal is still alive and capable.
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by a principal (muwakkil) to perform a specific task during the principal's lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what happens if a person appointed as executor (wasi) sells an item from the testator's estate without knowing he was appointed?
A) The sale is invalid because he lacked knowledge.
B) The sale is valid and binds him to the executorship.
C) The sale is valid only if the heirs consent.
D) The sale is suspended until he learns of the appointment.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an executor's sale is valid without his knowledge because executorship is succession (khilafah) akin to inheritance, whereas an agent's sale requires knowledge because agency is delegation (inabah).

Removal of a Treacherous Executor by the Qadi
Ruling on qadi dismissing a wasi due to khayanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a qadi may remove a wasi (executor) and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the testator's hypothetical action.

Core Idea
A qadi cannot dismiss an executor on mere complaint; only proven treachery (khayanah) justifies removal, as the qadi acts for the deceased.

This passage from the Book of Wills clarifies a crucial point about the authority of the Islamic judge (qadi) over executors (wasi). While heirs may sometimes wish to remove an executor, the qadi cannot act on suspicion alone—only clear evidence of betrayal allows replacement. The underlying principle is that the qadi steps into the testator's shoes: if the testator were alive and discovered the treachery, he would dismiss the executor himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What action is the passage discussing? (The qadi's removal of a wasi). What is the ruling? (Dismissal is obligatory when khayanah is proven, but not on mere complaint).
2
Distinguish valid and invalid causes
Why is a mere heir's complaint insufficient? Because the testator appointed the wasi based on trust; a complaint without proof does not establish a breach of that trust.
3
Trace the reasoning
How does the text justify the qadi's authority to dismiss? The qadi is the substitute (qaim maqam) of the deceased. If the testator were alive and knew of the treachery, he would dismiss the wasi himself. Since he cannot, the qadi acts in his place.
4
Note the consequence after dismissal
What happens after dismissal? The qadi appoints a new executor, and the original wasi is treated as if he never held the position.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Suppose an heir claims the wasi embezzled funds but provides no evidence. Can the qadi dismiss? No, because khayanah is not 'apparent' (zahir), and removal without proof is not permitted.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
۲۴۵
كتاب الوصايا
بات کے کہ جب خیانت ظاہر ہو جائے تو میت نے اس کو اس کی امانت کی وجہ سے وصی مقرر کیا تھا اور امانت فوت ہو چکی ہے اور اگر موصی زندہ لوگوں میں سے ہوتا تو اس کو وصیت سے خارج کر دیتا پس میت کے عاجز ہونے کے وقت قاضی اس کا قائم مقام ہو گا گویا کہ اس کا وصی ہے ہی نہیں ۔
تشریح اگر تمام ورثہ یا بعض ورثہ نے قاضی سے وصی کی شکایت کی تو اس کو وصایت سے خارج نہیں کرے گا البتہ اگر وصی کی خیانت ظاہر ہو جائے تو معزول کر دیا جائے گا کیونکہ وصی نے میت کی جانب سے ولایت حاصل کی ہے تو بلا وجہ قاضی کے لئے مناسب نہیں ہے کہ اس کو معزول کرے۔ ہاں اگر وصی کی خیانت ظاہر ہو جائے تو اور بات ہے لہذا اب اس کو معزول کر دیا جائے گا، کیونکہ موصی نے اس کو اس لئے اپنا وصی بنایا تھا کہ اس نے اس کو امانت دار سمجھا تھا اور اب اس کا پردہ فاش ہو گیا ہے لہذا اب اگر موصی زندہ ہوتا تو اس کو وصایت سے معزول کر دیتا تو اب جب کہ موصی وصایت سے خارج کرنے سے عاجز ہے تو قاضی اس کا قائم مقام ہو کر اس کو معزول کرے گا اور اس کی جگہ دوسرے کو مقرر کرے گا اور یوں سمجھیں گے گویا کہ میت کا کوئی وصی نہیں تھا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 19, page 245, Book of Wills. 
The point: When treachery becomes apparent, the deceased had appointed him as executor due to his trustworthiness, and the trust is now lost. If the testator were among the living, he would remove him from the executorship. So at the time of the deceased's inability, the qadi will stand in his place, as if he is not an executor at all.
Explanation: If all or some of the heirs complain to the qadi about the executor, he will not remove him from the executorship. However, if the executor's treachery becomes apparent, he will be dismissed. Because the executor has obtained authority from the deceased, so without cause it is not appropriate for the qadi to remove him. Yes, if the executor's treachery becomes apparent, it is a different matter. Therefore now he will be dismissed, because the testator had made him his executor because he considered him trustworthy, and now his veil has been torn. So now if the testator were alive, he would dismiss him from executorship. Now that the testator is unable to dismiss him from executorship, the qadi will stand in his place and dismiss him, and appoint another in his place, and they will consider as if the deceased had no executor.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a ruling passage explaining when a qadi may remove a wasi (executor). The key point is that mere complaint by heirs is not sufficient; the qadi requires actual evidence of treachery (khayanah) to dismiss the executor. The reasoning is that the testator appointed him based on trust; if that trust is breached, the testator would have dismissed him if alive. Since the testator cannot act, the qadi acts as his substitute. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the qadi has authority to manage matters the deceased cannot, and that dismissal requires a valid cause.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): Executor appointed by the testator to manage the will and estate.
خیانت (khayanah): Breach of trust, treachery, dishonesty in managing the estate.
قاضی (qadi): Islamic judge authorized to remove executors and appoint replacements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may a qadi remove a wasi (executor)?
A) Any time an heir complains
B) Only if the wasi requests removal
C) When the wasi's treachery becomes apparent
D) Only if the testator specified it in the will

Key Takeaway
A qadi may only remove a wasi upon clear evidence of treachery, acting as the testator's substitute to preserve trust.
